Sun Lianzhong's Army's Departure Postponed Again 73

But Troop Trains Have Been Urged to Wait for Transportation

Ma Hongkui Arrives in Jinan to Discuss Defense

Jinan Correspondence: Sun Lianzhong's 26th Route Army recently planned to depart on the 10th to suppress the communists in Jiangxi. However, as of the afternoon of that day, the government and various important figures had not received any telegrams regarding the actual departure of the army. Even the transportation department had not received any news from Jinan or Ning. According to Jinan and Ning telegrams, Sun's army began boarding the train on the morning of the 10th, but did not depart immediately. It was also heard that because Sun's army did not depart on the 5th, the Jinpu Railway changed the departure date to the 10th and borrowed a part of the seven troop trains transporting Sun's army to transport commercial goods between Yanzhou and Jinan. Because Sun's army was actually departing, they sent urgent telegrams to request the return of the trains. The Jinpu Railway returned the trains to Jinan and Ning in the afternoon of the 10th for Sun's army to use. However, on the 11th, the troops still had not departed, and those who had boarded the train got off again. Therefore, there is a saying here that Sun's army has temporarily postponed its departure.

Ma Hongkui, the commander-in-chief of the 15th Route Army, arrived in Jinan by special train from Tai'an at 8:10 pm on the 10th. Those traveling with him included Chief Counselor Hai Tao, Chief Secretary, Adjutant, and many others, as well as a platoon of guards. Li Zongbi, the chief of staff of the 3rd Route Army's General Headquarters, welcomed him at the station. After Li met with Ma, they took a car together to the Provincial Government to meet with Chairman Han Fuqu to discuss defense and bandit suppression. According to Ma, he had no important task in coming to Jinan this time. When reporters asked about the news of Sun Lianzhong's army's departure, he said that they had not yet departed. Li Zongbi also told reporters that part of Commander Sun's troops had departed some days ago, but the departure was not successful. They have not actually departed yet, but the date will not be delayed for too long. (11th)

The Process of Resolving the Reduction of the Jin Army 74

Determined to Follow the Tianjin Agreement

Separate Compilation of the Railway Protection Army and the Garrison

Taiyuan Correspondence: The news about the Jin Army's reduction has been widely spread and changed rapidly in the past few days. Not only are outsiders not aware of the truth, but even those involved in the matter have difficulty having a true and resolute opinion. At present, the Jin situation is indeed in a state where soldiers do not obey generals and the group is without a leader. Anyone who holds considerable strength naturally has his own considerable opinion. In addition, there must be meetings every day, and meetings must be deliberations. Since there are many opportunities for gatherings and discussions, new and newer opinions are easily generated. According to Ji Yiqiao, the different opinions of the Jin Army generals in the past few days mean that we, the personnel specially sent to supervise the demobilization, are often unsure. The complexity of its content can be seen. In summary, when the army commanders jointly sent telegrams, their fundamental opinions were about four points: (1) separation of military and civilian affairs, (2) phased demobilization, (3) abolition of the army commander system, and (4) changing the original ten armies of the Jin Army into ten divisions. The emergence of this opinion is partly because each army commander has his own factual difficulties, and partly because Shang, Xu, Yang, and Fu, who went to Tianjin to participate in the meeting, cannot but bear their considerable responsibilities. The crux of the matter has four points: (1) the army commanders believed that the four people, Shang et al., were all gloriously appointed as army commanders when they went to Tianjin, and those of us who did not go were all left out, (2) Shang Zhen was not only the chairman, but also the army commander and the director of the Civil Affairs Department, (3) Shang et al. did not solicit the opinions of the army commanders on the aftermath before leaving, and did not respect or accept the representations of the army commanders who had sent personnel to present their case several times upon their arrival in Tianjin, and (4) Shang, Xu, Yang, and Fu were appointed as army commanders, and the old army commanders were demoted to division commanders, and Li Fuying and Zhang Huizhao did not even have a division commander's position, so they were also dissatisfied. For these reasons, the Tianjin agreement could not be implemented smoothly. It was not until Xu Yongchang returned and mediated in many ways, coupled with the mediation of Song Zheyuan, Pang Bingxun, Zhang Hanjie, and Fu Cunhuai, that the two meetings of the headquarters were completed. The results obtained were only unilateral proposals. The final method still needs to be decided by the Northeast. Regarding the proposal of the military system, it was initially proposed to abolish the army commander system and take the division as the unit. The original ten armies were reduced to ten divisions, each division with six regiments, a total of sixty regiments, and compiled into the national army, directly subordinate to the Central Government. Then it was proposed to continue to follow the Tianjin agreement of four armies and eight divisions externally, and to still take the division as the unit internally, and to set up a military committee. Recently, it was proposed to compile a railway protection army and a garrison in addition to the four armies in accordance with the Tianjin agreement, each army with two divisions, each division with four regiments, and to set up three garrison commands in Taiyuan, southern Shanxi, and northern Shanxi, each command directly under the jurisdiction of two regiments. Whether the above three types can be implemented is another question, but they are still the relatively central opinions that have been formed after many meetings. Other large and small proposals are still too numerous to record. Until Jing Yaoyue, who was sent by the army commanders to Liaoning to meet with Zhang, returned and reported the true attitude of the Liaoning side, all parties believed that the general trend was irreversible and that the principle of the Tianjin agreement had to be adopted. Therefore, Shang, Xu, and Yang, together with Ji Yiqiao, Hu Yiling, and the representatives Sun Chu, Wang Jingguo, Yang Xiaoou, and Li Shengda, who were recommended by the army commanders and commanders, held a tripartite joint meeting at the Shanxi Hotel. After a long period of discussion, a final decision was made. As a result of the consultation, in addition to implementing the four armies and eight divisions system in accordance with the Tianjin agreement, the opinions of the army commanders were adopted to compile a railway protection army and a garrison. The military committee level was not discussed because it was an internal agency. The Jin situation, which had been in dispute for a long time, has now reached a considerable conclusion. The next day, Shang hosted a banquet for Ji, Hu, Xu, Yang, and the army commanders and commanders at his private residence. Everyone attended on time, which was quite a grand occasion. It was nominally a joint banquet, but it was no less than a celebration drama. In short, for the time being, it can certainly be said that the time is ripe.

As for the candidates for the army commanders and division commanders, the general decision is as follows: Shang Zhen, the commander of the 4th Army, is in charge of the two divisions of Yang Xiaoou and Feng Pengzhu; Xu Yongchang, the commander of the 5th Army, is in charge of the two divisions of Li Fuying and Yang Chengyuan; Yang Aiyuan, the commander of the 6th Army, is in charge of the two divisions of Yang Yaofang and Wang Jingguo; Fu Zuoyi, the commander of the 7th Army, is in charge of the two divisions of Li Shengda and Fu himself; Sun Chu is the commander of the Zhengtai Railway Protection Army, and Zhang Huizhao is the commander of the garrison. However, it was originally planned that the garrison would be directly under the jurisdiction of the garrison command, and Rong Honglu was planned to be the garrison commander. However, Rong told people that he was personally involved in this Jin situation dispute because he witnessed the elders of the three Jins being turned over and over in the mud, and his conscience could not bear it. Therefore, he did not hesitate to use his tongue to hope to pull them out of the water and put them on the mat. Personal honor and disgrace are not enough to be concerned about. Therefore, he has no intention of being the garrison commander proposed this time. However, he hopes that the elders of the three Jins have a reasonable solution so that he can feel at ease. For this reason, the garrison was assigned to Zhang Huizhao. As for the issue of taking office, Shang, Xu, and others advocated that the newly compiled army and division commanders should first send a telegram to take office, and then ask Deputy Commander Zhang for instructions on the decision-making measures. On the part of the generals, they insisted that after the plan decided by the consultations in recent days was telegraphed to the Northeast for approval and implementation, they would then send a telegram to take office, which seemed to be appropriate and appropriate. Therefore, on the 6th, the generals once again had a consultation at a certain commander's residence. It was heard that the principle was that they would take office at the same time after the Northeast approved it. (7th)

A Major Inspection is Held in Xuzhou 75

Forty-six Suspects of Smoking and Gambling are Arrested

Xuzhou Correspondence: Wang Jun, the commander of the Jinpu Garrison, recently convened a joint conference of local circles and decided to implement a major inspection, which was handed over to the Xuzhou Military Police Inspectorate for execution. The garrison headquarters first stipulated the inspection regulations. On the morning of the 11th, Chen Xueshun, the director of the Military Police Inspectorate, invited representatives from various agencies to set off separately. They were divided into three groups: the first group inspected the area around the West Gate, and Liu Ruifeng, the battalion commander of the 7th Division's Engineering Battalion, sent a company to accompany them on guard; the second group inspected the area around the North Gate, and Xiao Weiliang, the battalion commander of the 7th Division's Transport Battalion, sent two companies to accompany them on guard; the third group inspected the area around the East Railway Station, and because the area was wider, it was further divided into three small groups for implementation. Nie Jingpin, the battalion commander of the 2nd Battalion of the 38th Regiment of the 7th Division, led the entire battalion to accompany them on guard. In addition, each group was accompanied by a detachment sent by Yuan Zhengdong, the battalion commander of the 3rd Battalion of the Central Military Police stationed in Xuzhou, who was responsible for arresting criminals. The local police teams and public security teams were also divided into three groups to guide and guard. Eight officials from the Military Police Inspectorate and representatives from the county government, county party department, public security bureau, first district office, chamber of commerce, special party department of the 7th Division, and Jinpu Police Section, each led three groups of troops to carry out the inspection. The officials and representatives entered people's homes to inspect, and the military police troops waited outside the door. Along the roads inside and outside the city, the Engineering Battalion sent teams to add posts to make the inspection more thorough. The inspection was completed at noon, and temporary arrests were made. The first group arrested six people, the second group arrested six people, and the third group arrested thirty-four people. Statistics showed that suspects accounted for 40%, smokers and gamblers accounted for 20%, and the rest were mostly idle soldiers and discharged wounded soldiers, who were sent to the Military Police Inspectorate for interrogation. Director Chen plans to have ordinary criminals checked by various districts for bail, while military criminals will be submitted to the garrison headquarters for handling. The precautions for this inspection are: 1. weapons, 2. reactionary publications, 3. poisons, 4. idle personnel, and 5. prostitutes, gamblers, thieves, and bandits. The township heads and village chiefs will also guide the inspection to ensure familiarity and thoroughness. (February 11th)

Eight Counties in Guangdong Province Implement the New County System 76

The Civil Affairs Department Formulates Matters for the Implementation of the New System

The Finance Department Stipulates the Local Autonomy Expenses

Guangzhou Correspondence: In order to implement local autonomy, the Guangdong Civil Affairs Department plans to designate eight major counties to start a pilot program from March 1st. Preparations for the implementation of the new county system have been drafted in recent days. Once the provincial affairs meeting makes a resolution, it can be implemented.

Page 10

It is found that the eight counties for the new county system pilot program are Nanhai, Chaoan, Shunde, Taishan, Huiyang, Gaoyao, Qiongshan, and Qujiang. After the new county system is implemented, according to the new organizational law, the original police districts will be changed to public security sub-bureaus or sub-stations, which will be under the jurisdiction of the county public security bureau. The county public security bureau chief will be concurrently held by the county magistrate. After the county public security bureau is established, the entire county's guards or self-defense forces will be directed and supervised by the public security bureau. Therefore, the power of the county magistrate under the new system is greater than the power of the old county magistrate. As for the county autonomy expenses, the Finance Department also planned yesterday to designate funds so that autonomy matters can be fully implemented. According to the opinion of the Finance Department, the provincial treasury's income is not enough to cover expenses. If these autonomy expenses are allocated from the provincial treasury's taxes, other government expenses will inevitably be impossible to maintain. It is necessary to raise other funds. In February of this year, the department drafted a method for adding local taxes to counties before the land tax is changed, as well as regulations for the collection of township and town field and land donations, which were also approved for trial implementation. The original method for adding taxes was changed from the 19th year of the Republic of China. All local taxes added by various departments were incorporated into the original Dingmi unified tax amount, and a single collection was made without setting up additional names. The tax rate for unified collection was also changed by converting the odd amounts into whole amounts. The total income was divided into ten parts, with two parts retained and allocated as county local autonomy expenses, and the remaining eight parts were submitted to the department. It was also stated in the proposed regulations for the township and town field and land donations that they were for raising funds for township and town autonomy and other public security, education, and agricultural improvement needs. Now that various counties are carrying out autonomy, they should be allocated separately within the two established methods. All counties have been strictly ordered to follow these regulations. (8th)

Salt Surtax Still Collected in Northern Anhui 77

The Finance Department Appoints Zhao Chunpu as the New Director of the Collection Bureau

Bengbu Correspondence: The Anhui Provincial General Bureau for the Collection of Salt Surtax in Northern Anhui was established in Bengbu last month under orders, but it has not been implemented due to unanimous opposition from merchants and people. Although the Su County sub-bureau superficially collects a surtax of 1.5 yuan per dan of salt, the salt merchants use a registration method to temporarily record the accounts as a wait-and-see attitude. Therefore, there is actually no money to collect. Since the Bengbu General Bureau has no money to collect and has spent more than 2,000 yuan of start-up funds received from the province in more than a month, the director, Duan Shizhang, recently claimed illness and submitted his resignation to the Finance Department, which was approved. The Finance Department then appointed Zhao Chunpu as the acting director. (Zhao is currently the deputy director of the Adjutant's Office of the Reserve Army Corps and concurrently the director of the Corps' Office in Bengbu.) After Duan left Bengbu, the various departments in the bureau have been handling the handover in recent days. It is heard that Zhao will soon come to Bengbu from the province to take over. The Anhui Provincial Government will not stop the salt surtax collection because of the Central Government's repeated orders to stop it. Therefore, the hope of the merchants and people of northern Anhui to abolish the salt surtax is not easy to realize for a while. (February 10th)

New Regulations of the Qingdao Commodity Inspection Bureau 78

New Regulations of the Commodity Inspection Bureau

Qingdao Correspondence: The Qingdao Commodity Inspection Bureau, in accordance with the instructions of the Ministry of Industry, will begin inspecting cotton on the 9th of this month. The detailed inspection rules have been stipulated by the bureau and are recorded as follows: (Article 1) These detailed rules are based on Article 22 of the Provisional Regulations on Commodity Inspection. (Article 2) When a merchant or firm fills out the inspection application form in accordance with Article 2, Paragraph 1 of the Cotton Inspection Regulations, the merchant's address or the firm's location, trademark or symbol, package, quality, origin, quantity, weight, stack name and location, departure date, ship name, destination, consignee's name, and firm, etc., must be filled in separately. (Article 3) The Commodity Inspection Bureau shall complete the cotton inspection procedures within two days after sampling. If a Sunday or holiday is encountered, the time will be extended accordingly. However, in case of necessity, work may be carried out as usual. (Article 4) The certificate for the purchase and sale in the distribution market is valid for two months from the date of issuance. However, it may be extended for two months at the request of the reporter. (Article 5) Merchants or firms that report less than 100 catties of cotton shall pay the inspection fee according to 100 catties. (Article 6) If a merchant or firm loses a certificate, in addition to applying to the bureau for a replacement certificate in accordance with Article 15 of the Provisional Regulations on Commodity Inspection, the original certificate number and the circumstances of the loss shall be published in the local newspaper for two days to declare it invalid. If the Commodity Inspection Bureau deems it necessary to re-inspect the goods for which the certificate was lost, it may be re-inspected. (Article 7) If a merchant or firm has one of the following circumstances, he may submit a written request together with the original certificate to the bureau for verification and exchange: (1) the goods are repackaged, (2) the customs declaration for export is overdue, (3) the ship is changed, (4) the export date is changed, (5) the repackaging quantity is changed, (6) the certificate is damaged, (7) other reasons for which the certificate must be exchanged. (Article 8) When applying for a replacement certificate or applying for an exchange certificate in accordance with the preceding article, a fee of five jiao in national currency must be paid for each certificate. (Article 9) These detailed rules shall be implemented from the date of approval by the Ministry of Industry. (February 8th)

Hangzhou Express Letter 79

The Ningbo and Hangzhou Rice Industry Associations have successively petitioned the provincial government to exempt the food industry from the 1/1000 business tax in order to alleviate the people's livelihood and reduce the burden, but this has not been approved. Therefore, they have separately requested the Hangzhou Chamber of Commerce to convey the commercial situation, sincerely requesting exemption. The Municipal Chamber of Commerce has already submitted a report based on the situation, and the standing committee has visited Director Wang of the Finance Department in person to explain in detail the impossibility of increasing taxes. It is heard that there is a proposal to change the tax to be collected according to the total amount of capital.

The Hangzhou Municipal Chamber of Commerce wrote to various industry associations stating that it had received an order from the municipal government approving a letter from the Hangzhou County Executive Committee stating that the price of rice in Hangzhou City has been stable, and all commodity prices that have increased due to the impact of rice prices should be reduced accordingly in order to achieve balance. Please all industry stores comply with this order.

The Finance Department received a total of five telegrams from the Shaoxing Foil Industry Association, and one telegram each from foil merchants Ru Shibao and Wang Yuanchang, all regarding the matter of subscribing for the foil business tax. A reply was given yesterday, stating that since the Shaoxing Foil Industry Association is responsible for proving that the subscription for the special business tax on foil in Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces is thorough and open, it is completely different from the previous contract donation system. Moreover, the department will still appoint a director to set up a bureau to supervise the collection. In the future, strict supervision will be carried out to ensure that the subscribing merchants do not manipulate and confuse the situation. If the foil shop industry believes that the collection procedures are not in accordance with the regulations, they are allowed to report the facts to the bureau for verification.

The Provincial Women's Sericulture Training Institute is currently proposed to be cancelled by the Construction Department. After a resolution by the Political Committee, it is scheduled to be closed on the 15th. The original 140 female students in the institute will register for screening at the Women's Sericulture Training Department attached to the Provincial Sericulture Improvement Center to determine who will stay and who will leave. An order has been issued to the center to comply. (12th)

Wuxi 81

Dr. Tao Chishun Accidentally Kills a Patient: Zhang Shouying, the wife of Zhou Jingxiao, a resident of the county, suffered from liver and stomach problems. On the 23rd of last month, Zhou invited Dr. Tao Chishun, the director of Housheng Hospital, to his home to take her pulse. Dr. Tao prescribed a bottle of stomach medicine and told Zhou to purchase a bottle of "Ovarian Afu'er" medication. He arrived at Zhou's home at 7 PM the following evening to administer an intravenous injection. However, as soon as the needle was withdrawn, Zhang's face turned pale, she sweated profusely, cried out in pain, her eyes rolled upward, she foamed at the mouth, and her limbs trembled, rendering her speechless. Upon seeing this, Tao immediately instructed Zhou to summon Western doctors Qian Baohua and Xu Shilin to his home for emergency treatment. Dr. Xu Shilin drew urine for examination and determined that the needle had touched a toxic substance, causing it to enter the bloodstream, making recovery impossible. Subsequently, Cheng Zhongfu and others were invited for emergency treatment, but it was ineffective. Zhang died tragically at noon on the 26th. Zhou immediately telegraphed Zhang's family in Dongtai. Zhang’s brother, Zaiyang, and others received the telegram and suspected that Zhou had failed to provide proper medical treatment, leading to her death. Zhou, feeling helpless, visited Dr. Tao's residence and requested him to come to his home to certify the cause of death in order to dispel public doubt. Unexpectedly, Tao's father, Tingfang, actually filed a lawsuit against Zhou in the county court, accusing him of damaging his reputation and trespassing on his residence. The court has now scheduled a hearing for the 23rd of this month to question Zhou. Zhou has also engaged lawyers An Ruotai and Yang Shi to draft a counter-suit against Tao Chishun, accusing him of negligence and manslaughter. Zhou is a reporter for the Xin Wuxi Bao (New Wuxi News) and a member of the Journalists' Union. Yesterday, he reported the details of the incident to the Union, requesting assistance. After receiving the report, the Union convened an emergency meeting of its members. From the perspective of the journalistic community, it was determined that justice should be upheld and humanity maintained in the case of a quack doctor causing death. It was resolved to form a specialized committee to determine six measures, issue a declaration, arouse public opinion, and sanction quack doctors who cause death. Sun Dexian, Song Shuqin, Shi Qinglin, and eleven others were appointed as committee members to handle the case. An official letter was sent to the County Physicians' Association, requesting them to hold a meeting to study the case, provide a detailed explanation, and respond impartially. Separate letters were sent to the doctors who had previously treated the patient, requesting detailed explanations. In addition, a petition was submitted to the County Party Committee and the County Government, urging them to uphold justice and impose the appropriate punishment on the quack doctor Tao Chishun. Furthermore, a renowned Shanghai physician was invited as a consultant to study the case, and the legal advisor to the Union was consulted to study the legal aspects of the proceedings.

Crackdown on Lu Changxing's Illegal Profiteering: Lu Changxing's cigarette paper shop in Xiatang, Qingming Bridge, outside the South Gate, has been engaged in the business of mortgaging gold and silver jewelry for several years. Its business has been very good, attracting the attention of bandits. In the past two years, two robbery cases have occurred. Recently, someone filed a complaint with the county government, accusing the shop of corruption. The county magistrate ordered the Third Branch of the Public Security Bureau to thoroughly investigate the matter. After investigation and verification by Director Wang Weixin of the Bureau, it was found that the shop's concurrent operation of gold and silver jewelry was aimed at seeking illicit profits, which was highly inappropriate. Yesterday, the county government ordered the Bureau to effectively crack down on the illegal business.

Public Inspection of Electricity Theft at the New World: Recently, the Qishuyan Power Plant, in order to strictly prevent users from stealing electricity, organized an inspection team and dispatched investigators to conduct inspections. Recently, suspicious points were found on the seal of the yellow paper seal outside the electricity meter of the New World Hotel. The box was cut off and sealed by the Second Branch of the Public Security Bureau for resolution. Subsequently, Zhang Deqing and Xie Shaojing, the managers of the New World Hotel, negotiated with the Chamber of Commerce and the Qishuyan Power Plant and jointly agreed on the following two points: (1) Both parties shall each send representatives to conduct a public inspection at the County Chamber of Commerce to prove the authenticity of the number and signature image on the seal. The Chamber of Commerce representative shall serve as a notary, and the County Government representative shall serve as an observer. (2) Representatives from both parties shall take the sealed electricity meter to the Shanghai Municipal Government Public Utilities Bureau for verification to prove whether the meter is running fast or slow. On the afternoon of the previous day, a public inspection was conducted at the Chamber of Commerce. The attendees included Na Menglin from the County Government, Qian Sunqing and Na Tongyi from the County Chamber of Commerce, Li Boshen, Zhu Zhilun, Yang Huaigu, Li Jizeng, and Yang Da from the Qichang Factory, and Zhang Deqing and Xie Shaojing from the New World. The electricity meter sealed by the Second Branch of the Public Security Bureau was also sent for inspection. After reviewing the meter, the attendees found no errors. The yellow paper seal and the small seal were repeatedly studied, and three suspicious points were identified: (1) The Arabic numerals used to arrange the numbers seemed to have different sizes, and the shape of the "0" was also different. (2) There seemed to be a doubt in the "Zeng" character in Li Jizeng's signature. (3) The hidden marks on the seal could not be identified. After the representatives of both parties discussed these three points for a long time, the box was reopened for inspection of the electricity meter. After a detailed inspection, no obvious flaws could be found. It was agreed to reseal the original box, sign by the representatives of both parties, and temporarily store it at the Chamber of Commerce pending resolution.

His five-year-old son, Shao Rong, was kidnapped by bandits on the afternoon of November 18th last year. Later, Gu Arong, a fellow villager living with him, contacted the bandits and redeemed the hostage for 2,000 yuan. It was later discovered that Gu Arong was the kidnapper in this case and had fled back to Changzhou and was hiding in his home. Fengxian 83

Order to Prepare for the Establishment of the County Land Bureau: The county government, in response to instructions from the Civil Affairs and Finance Departments regarding the land survey and measurement case, was authorized to prepare for the establishment of the Fengxian County Land Bureau in advance. The bureau would be responsible for handling all necessary start-up and monthly administrative matters. All expenses would be raised by the county on a monthly basis until the land survey fee could be collected. However, the request to establish a preparatory land survey committee was not approved. It is now understood that the case has been submitted to the current County Administrative Council for discussion. It is planned to levy a special donation of five cents per mu starting from the busy season of the 20th year for surveying, exchanging documents, and registering, with a three-year period. This is expected to raise 157,800 yuan. Changshu 84

The Truth About the Kidnapping Case at Maojia Bridge: Shen Tongshun Oil Mill at Maojia Bridge, about four li outside Shuibeimen, was robbed on the 27th of last month, and the shop owner Yao Shou and his partner Xue Guanxing were kidnapped. It is now rumored in the community that Yao's kidnapping involved fraud, as Yao and others could not afford to pay the ransom. Some say they are still in the bandits' den. To investigate the details, the reporter went to the countryside for an on-site investigation and met Yao Shou's nephew, Shen Shengsheng. According to him, his uncle (Yao Shou) and Guanxing were indeed kidnapped by bandits on the 27th of last month and escaped on the 31st. Yao recounted the incident, saying that when he was kidnapped by the bandits, he pleaded for his release, but to no avail. He was hidden in the bow of the boat, preventing him from seeing the daylight. There were a total of three bandit boats, and the boat hiding Yao was in the middle of the two boats, guarded by eight bandits. During the day, they often patrolled in the river near Guangsheng Bridge, and at night they anchored in a small river. This lasted for two days. On the night of the 30th, the boat anchored somewhere, and all eight bandits went ashore. The boatman, who had been rowing all day, was extremely tired and fell asleep as soon as he lay down, snoring loudly. His uncle (Yao) saw an opportunity and used a bamboo pole to pole the boat to the other shore. He and Xue Guanxing left the boat and ran, crossing villages and wading through water. They did not know how many places they had been. Because they were eager to escape danger, they traveled all night. When dawn was approaching, they realized they had reached Tangjia Bridge. They knocked on the door of a village house and told the owner what had happened. The owner was very sympathetic and allowed them to stay for the whole day, fearing that they would encounter bandits again if they traveled at night. That night, they returned to their hometown. Fortunately, they were unharmed. However, due to the severe shock, their health was not good, and they are still unable to see guests. As for the rumors outside that the incident was fraudulent, it was actually a misunderstanding.

The 14th District Office Judged a Missing Person Case as Death: Chen Xirong, a hired worker from Tan Jiajijiren, Tiandu Township, 14th District, at the home of Zhang Yuanheng, Xujiacun, Ma Zhen Yaoduntou Township, suddenly died of abdominal pain in the middle of the night after working at Zhang's house for four or five years. Bandit Wang Shaowen Executed by Firing Squad: On the 27th of last month, officers of the Detective Team arrested Wang Shaowen, a resident bandit, from Zhongjiatai, outside of the city. He confessed that he held an important position in the bandit gang, that he had traveled to Shanghai to purchase twelve Browning pistols to bring back for a riot, and that he had repeatedly led bandits to hold weapons and plunder, extorting money. The county government reported this to the provincial government. Yesterday (the 11th) at 2 pm, a cable was received approving the death penalty. At around 5 pm, he was taken out and tied up by the river in front of Wang Gongheng's house on Hebei Street, east of the city, where he was executed by firing squad.

Sentencing in the Case of the Shooting of Political Police: Dai Hong, Dai Yu, and Wu Kui, political police officers of the county government, were traveling to Xiaoling Township on official business on September 2, 1928. The bandits ordered them to stop, swarmed onto the boat, and upon seeing that they were political police officers from the county government, tied them up with ropes, carried them ashore, and shot them dead. The county government has now rendered its judgment: Zhu Youcheng and Zhong Chunzhao are sentenced to life imprisonment and deprivation of civil rights for life. Zhong Zhu's family is sentenced to imprisonment for one year and eight months. The number of days of detention before sentencing is deducted from the imprisonment, with two days of detention equivalent to one day of imprisonment. Civil rights are deprived for three years.

He had been living at home for over a year without any means of livelihood. Furthermore, as the end of winter approached, creditors were pressing him for payment. Recovery of the Yu Da Warehouse and Storage of Funds: After the establishment of the Xiaoshan County Warehouse Management Committee, it was decided that the old Yu Da Warehouse, which was occupied by the Public Security Bureau, should be vacated by the Public Security Bureau by a set date, as ordered by the county government. Personnel were sent to take over, assess, and repair the warehouse. The expenses would be paid from the public accumulated interest funds stored in the old Yu Da Warehouse. As for the 7,000 yuan of public bonds stored in the Yu Da Warehouse, which had a face value of 1,000 yuan each, it was decided to exchange them for 20 bonds with a face value of 100 yuan each, at 2,000 yuan each, with those who held such public bonds. The remaining 5,000 yuan was converted into 500 bonds with a face value of 10 yuan each, with the original serial numbers retained. Members were sent out to raise cash. In addition, Committee Member Xiang Fan was sent to take over the warehouse.

The funds were originally a batch of military rice purchased by Chairman Chiang Kai-shek in Gaohebu Town, Anhui Province, the year before last. Before it could be transported, a rice shortage broke out in Wan Yuan. It was then approved to retain the rice to help the people. Jin was in charge of selling the rice. Later, Cheng Tianfang and others from the Anhui Provincial Committee presented a request to Chairman Chiang Kai-shek to donate the funds for the construction of the Sun Yat-sen Memorial Hall in Anqing. Education News

Important News

Ministry of Education Orders Rectification of the Three Major Universities in Beiping 92

Specifies Five Areas for Improvement

Yesterday, the Ministry of Education, upon the order of the Executive Yuan, stipulated the matters that should be improved in the administrative affairs of the three universities in Beijing, Beiping Normal University. The three universities were officially ordered to comply with the order, which stated: "Report from the Chairman of the National Government on the inspection of various universities in Beiping is issued, generally opening that: when going to visit the schools, those in charge are mostly not in school, the number of teachers in various schools is surprisingly large, teachers take part-time jobs outside the school, one person is the department head of several schools, thereby being absent from class, is considered commonplace, student in class are listless, there are not even a third of the students in class, equipment is very lacking, the machines are damaged, the library is also mostly in name only. In terms of expenses, salaries often account for more than eight-tenths of the total budget, while equipment costs are less than one-tenth. Students occupy dormitories, treating them as their own property and passing them on privately, etc. School administration and academic atmosphere are declining to this point, which is extremely distressing. The above situation, although not necessarily all possessed by each school, gradually accumulates into habits, and it is difficult to avoid mutual infection. If it is not strictly rectified, how can it be worthy of the state's intention to educate and cultivate talents? Now, the following matters that should be improved first in the administrative affairs of Beijing and Beiping Normal University are stipulated below:"

(1) The equipment of each school should be strengthened as much as possible, the funds should be properly allocated, the percentage of salaries should be reduced, and the percentage of equipment should be increased. The existing equipment of each school should also be carefully maintained, and should not be allowed to be discarded or disordered.

(2) The part-time jobs of teachers should be strictly limited, and one person may not hold the position of director or full-time teacher in two places. The part-time jobs of full-time teachers should comply with the Ministry's orders, limited to six hours per week, and must obtain the prior consent of the principal of the original school.

(3) Rules should be established and strictly implemented regarding the investigation of students' attendance in class.

(4) Rules should be clearly defined and strictly enforced regarding various examinations of students.

(5) School affairs must be earnestly rectified, students must no longer be allowed to occupy dormitories and privately transfer them, and it is forbidden to allow outsiders to stay. Violators will be punished or expelled.

The above items are only the most essential ones. The principals of each school are still expected to carefully examine, earnestly rectify, and seek improvement in all matters that each school should develop and reform. In addition to separate orders, this order is hereby issued for compliance and to report on the handling situation for review. This order.

Report on the Ministry of Education's Innovation Work 93

January of the 20th Year

(I) Higher Education

(I) Expediting Verification of Graduate Transcripts and Certificates from Colleges and Above: A circular was issued to all public and private colleges and above, instructing them to submit transcripts and certificates of graduates for record and verification within one month after the end of the semester. Schools that had not submitted verification documents for the 18th year were given a deadline of one month from the date of the document's arrival to submit them to the Ministry. Schools that had not submitted verification documents for the 16th and 17th years were required to prepare supplementary resumes and transcripts for record. Graduates before the establishment of private schools should be handled in accordance with Announcement No. 8 of the 19th year.

(II) Investigation of Names and Addresses of Private Colleges and Above Throughout the Country: A circular was issued to all provincial and municipal departments and bureaus, requesting them to investigate and report the names, addresses, etc., of all private colleges and above within their jurisdictions.

(III) Approval of Establishment of Private Schools: Approval was granted to merge the Education College of the private Fujian Union University and to establish it under the name of the private Fujian Union College. The private Fujian Law and Politics Vocational School was granted the same treatment as already established private schools.

(IV) Issuance of Study Abroad Certificates: Approval was granted to issue public-funded study abroad certificates to one person to study in Italy and one person to study in France. Approval was granted to issue self-funded study abroad certificates to a total of fifty-three people, including four to the United States, four to Germany, four to France, five to Belgium, one to the Philippines, and thirty-five to Japan.

Two Instructions from the Jiangsu Education Department 94

Order to County Education Bureaus to Report Statistics on School-Age Children

丨Order Regarding Leave Application Procedures for Directors of Social Education Institutions丨

Order 1: Instruction No. 285 from the Jiangsu Provincial Department of Education to the Directors of County Education Bureaus states: The investigation of school-age children is of great importance to the implementation of compulsory education. Previous orders from the Ministry have been issued for investigation and filling out forms, and repeated urging has been done. It is now found that the deadline for compiling and reporting the statistical tables of school-age children for the 18th year has long passed. Many counties have already reported, but many others have been delaying. This matter concerns an investigation and filling-out of forms ordered by the Ministry. How can we allow further delay? In addition to issuing separate orders urging reporting, we hereby urgently order the director of the bureau to promptly submit a report within ten days of receiving this document for compilation and forwarding. Do not delay. This order.

Order 2: Instruction No. 276 from the Jiangsu Provincial Department of Education to Provincial Social Education Institutions states: The procedures for leave application for principals of provincial primary and secondary schools have been clearly stipulated by this Department. "One may not leave one's post without reporting and applying for leave. If leaving school for a week or more, one should designate a representative to be responsible and act on one's behalf. The representative must also be reported to the Department of Education for record," etc. After the articles of service were stipulated, we have complied and implemented them. Directors of various social education institutions are in charge of the administrative responsibilities of their respective institutions. This should be done in the same way and they should not leave their posts arbitrarily. Hereafter, the regulations for leave application should immediately apply to the regulations for principals of primary and secondary schools. In addition to issuing separate orders, we hereby order compliance. This order.

Municipal Education Bureau Issues Order to Strengthen Military Education 96

Shanghai Municipal Education Bureau Instruction No. 178: Order to all high schools and above in this city (no separate document will be issued). Case: The Ministry of Education's Instruction No. 167 states, "Case: The revised military education plan for high schools and above stipulates that military education should be studied for two years, two hours per week each year. This Ministry has already issued orders for compliance. It is now found that since the implementation of military training in public and private secondary schools and above in various provinces and cities, many have complied with the orders, but many have also disregarded them. Some schools only teach military subjects for one hour per week, while others reduce the time for practical training and increase the number of years of study. Moreover, uniforms are often incomplete, and morale is lax. Such situations hinder the progress of military training education. It must be known that military education is of great importance. The principals of each school are responsible for guidance and should supervise the equipment and teaching time of military education at all times, and should follow the provisions of laws and regulations and handle it seriously, and there should be no more habits of procrastination and disagreement. Furthermore, student uniform regulations have long been promulgated. Students should wear uniforms during military training to show neatness and should not ask for leave on the pretext of hindering teaching progress. In addition to issuing separate orders, we hereby order the bureau to notify public and private high schools and above to be aware of this order," etc. Upon receiving this order, we have already issued orders regarding the Ministry's revised military education plan for high schools and above and student uniform regulations. Now, upon receiving the previous instructions, we hereby order all high schools and above in this city to comply with this order. This order, February of the 20th year of the Republic of China, Xu Peihuang, Director of the Shanghai Municipal Education Bureau.

He has now obtained a Master of Arts degree. His thesis is "The Value of Empiricism in the History of American Literary Criticism," which has been highly praised. It is said that it will be published by the Minzhi Bookstore in this city. He once entered his work "Liang," which he wrote at one time, in last year's Western American Poetry Competition and won the second prize, hence the name of poet. When Guang Dong Xian wrote a poem attacking an American woman, Zhang Jun published a paper on the matter in the Los Angeles Times, which was well received by the American people. He has now left the United States and is scheduled to arrive in Shanghai on February 19.

Laugh It Off · Sea · Guest

A丨I have been married for ten years. Only now can my wife and I be considered a true couple. B丨That's strange. What do you mean?

A丨Only because for ten years, my wife has always complained that I am too fat, which makes me angry.

B丨You are too fat, aren't you?

A丨But she doesn't say I'm fat anymore, and I don't care if she complains or not. I absolutely don't get angry. So I say only now can we be considered a true couple.

Teacher (examining a student's calligraphy book.)丨Child, I think your handwriting is a bit unreliable.

Student丨Teacher, how is it unreliable?

Teacher丨I don't think you wrote this because it's too good.

Student丨Teacher, I really wrote it. Am I not allowed to improve?

Teacher丨You can't improve that quickly. Tell me honestly, did your sister write it for you?

Student (ashamed and timid)丨Teacher, no, no, she didn't. I borrowed my sister's pen to write it.

Philanthropist (visiting a women's prison, led by a prison official to tour the rooms.)丨Are there many female prisoners here?

Prison Official丨Too many. It's simply overcrowded.

Philanthropist (passing a room, he catches sight of two women in it, dressed neatly.)丨Oh. Those two female prisoners are dressed very neatly.

Prison Official丨I'm sorry. These are my two daughters. This room is not a prison cell.

Wu Men Anecdotes 107

By Fan·Niu·Weng·

Gu Erniang Carves Inkstones: During the early Qing Dynasty, in the Shunzhi reign, Gu Erniang of Wu (Suzhou) was skilled at carving stone inkstones, inheriting her family's craft. She carved with meticulous detail and possessed unique artistic insight. Ordinary stones in her hands could be transformed into works of art. She could even use her small bound feet to test the quality of the stone. Tu Yuyang, the Shàngshū (High Official) of Xincheng, visited Su (Suzhou) and called on Song Muzhong, the Zhōngchéng (Censor), admiring Erniang's reputation. He sent attendants to her home in Zhuanzhu Lane, Jin Chang Ting, requesting her to carve several inkstones. This event is recorded in Yuyang's "Poetry Talks," "Ancient Fuyu Pavilion Miscellany," and "Chibei Outskirts Talks," mentioned repeatedly. Her skill can thus be understood. Today, Gu's descendants still uphold the family business, carefully polishing and restoring the inkstones. However, the current granddaughter-in-law's bound feet are like lotus boats on the peak of Taiyi Mountain—not three inches, but ten feet long.

Jin Shengtan Becomes the Mountain God of Dengwei: Zhang Ruocai, whose courtesy name was Shouhe, was extraordinarily intelligent. He lived in Liujia Port, inside Changmen (Suzhou City Gate), with a modestly prosperous family. His home boasted a beautiful bamboo and wood pavilion. The plaque of Guanhua Hall was inscribed by Chen Meigong Jiru of Songjiang. After the Shunzhi Emperor entered the customs, Ruocai, along with Jin Renrui, initially sought to participate in the provincial examination, hoping to eat芹(celery, symbolizing success in examinations). Thus, Zhang Ruocai transformed into Jin Shengtan. In his daily life, he drank and feigned madness, looking down on everyone else. He would take Zhuangzi, Lisao, Records of the Grand Historian, Du Fu's poems, Shi Nai'an's Water Margin, and Wang Shifu's Romance of the Western Chamber, reading and critiquing them. He praised them as the "Six Books of Talented Scholars," implying that apart from these six books, there was nothing else worth reading. Such was his extravagance. In the eighteenth year of Shunzhi, Shengtan was forty-three. In July, the tragic edict arrived in Su (Suzhou). Officials, as per custom, went to the Taiyang Palace to wail and mourn. Shengtan had once offended the Provincial Governor Zhu Guozhi with his words. Zhu held a deep-seated grudge and, taking advantage of the "alarming edict," fabricated charges against fourteen students, including Bai Gui and Zhang Jin, imprisoning them and sentencing them to death. In October, the details were sealed and sent to the capital for review. They were escorted to the imperial ruins (the imperial ruins were located in front of the Yanzi Temple. Zhang Shicheng built palaces there when he occupied Wu (Suzhou). Inside was Qiyun Tower. Xu Da and Chang Yuchun destroyed Suzhou and burned Qiyun Tower, which was at this location, leaving scorched earth, hence the name "ruins.") for execution. As Shengtan was about to be executed, he laughed and said to the executioner, "Beheading is the most painful thing, and confiscation is the most tragic thing. I, Jin Shengtan, never thought I would obtain it unintentionally. It can also be called a unique event in history.” After his death, his wife and children were exiled to Ningguta (His son was named Chao Gong and had a collection of literary works). His friend Wang Zhuoshan, from the same county and village, used planchette writing to summon the spirit of Shengtan, who came and wrote four poems.

"The vast world, past and present, is like floating dust.

All who are born, egg-born, are like dreams.

Only Jin Sheng cannot sleep,

And composes poetry under ten thousand plum blossoms."

He also added a note: "I have received grace from the Heavenly Emperor and have been appointed as the Copper Pit God of Dengwei Mountain!" (Dengwei is also called Xuanmu. Scholars all make a living by planting plum trees. There are no other trees for thirty miles. When Song Muzhong Mantang, the Provincial Governor of Suzhou, was in Shangqiu, he inscribed the three characters "Fragrant Snow Sea" on a stele at the Situ Temple, which still exists today.)

Relief for Divorce in Romania 108

By Lü·Bing·

In recent years, divorce cases have been emerging endlessly in countries around the world. This trend is prevalent in the United States and has spread to the European continent. The relationship between men and women, sometimes together and sometimes apart, is viewed as normal and is not subject to any restrictions. It is now reported that Romania has already established divorce laws to remedy the situation. After implementation, the trend of advocating divorce in society should be slightly curbed.

The latest marriage law was drafted by Minister of Justice Dr. Qiuning. Severe penalties are to be imposed for abandonment and breach of contract between men and women. For example, if a husband abandons his wife at home and lives away for a long time, or if a wife arbitrarily leaves her husband without living together, fines or imprisonment shall be imposed in accordance with the law. The term of imprisonment is approximately three months to one year. In addition, the law also stipulates heavy fines for issues related to extramarital affairs. If a man and woman have entered into a marriage contract, and one party suddenly requests termination for some reason, the return of gifts and tokens should go through legal procedures and not be privately exchanged between the two parties. The protection for men and women who have entered into a marriage contract is even more comprehensive. The engagement ring is as important as the wedding ring in law. Furthermore, if a woman is rejected, she must still have her former fiancé's name attached to her name until she finds a second lover and enters into a marriage contract before she can break free. In addition, the new law also includes provisions for the benefit of illegitimate children. Illegitimate children are registered with their biological father's surname. If they are abandoned and the father is found, all education and other expenses can be pursued and enforced by law.

Wu Xingfen's Witty Remarks on Painting 109

By Zheng Yimei

In recent painting circles, there are many female painters, such as Wu Xingfen, Zhang Hongwei, Fan Yingchu, Gu Qingyao, and Wu Qingxia, among whom Xingfen is a giant. It is unfortunate to hear of her passing away. Her virtuous voice is not far away, and there are still those who can describe her in general terms. Xingfen once discussed painting with others, saying that the quality of painting does not lie in being rough or fine. There should be fine intentions in roughness, and there should be sketch intentions in fineness. That is the best. When painting grass, insects, birds, and animals, one should seek their interest and charm, not their exact likeness. Exact likeness is best achieved in animal specimens. Why bother seeking it in painting? Among paintings, flowers and plants are the easiest, and figures are the most difficult. Therefore, those who paint for guests mostly paint flowers and plants and rarely paint figures. However, among figures, Amitabha Buddha is also particularly easy to paint. A triangular Zongzi (glutinous rice dumpling) with a longan on top embodies the Buddha state. While speaking, she painted it, her wit being such. When asked about contemporary trends of including foreign flowers and exotic animals in paintings, she responded, "Ancient people painted based on sketching from life. What didn't exist in ancient times could not be painted by ancient people. What is commonly seen today can be painted by modern people." Those who heard this were amazed. Xingfen also said, "Painting is related to one's character. Those with high character will have paintings that are free and unrestrained. Those with low character will have paintings that are inferior and turbid. Therefore, it is better to discuss one's character than to discuss one's painting.” Xingfen had a female companion who asked Xingfen to paint a peach. Xingfen was lazy and did not paint it even after frequent requests. The companion felt it was difficult to urge her again. However, her desire to obtain it was very urgent. One day, someone gifted her a basket of Feicheng peaches. The Feicheng peach has red flesh and thin skin. When the skin is slightly broken, the juice flows out, and one can suck it clean, leaving only the skin and pit. It is a famous product of Shandong Province. Xingfen was delighted when she ate it and remembered the peach painting. She painted it immediately as a reward. Her inspired brushstrokes were extraordinary. The companion treasured it like a gem.

The Vow of White Heads 110

By Zui·Chi·Sheng·

"We two are bound by a vow of white heads," these high-sounding words, full of happy colors, can often be seen in the newspaper announcements of couples getting engaged. "White heads" mean "growing old together." It is truly right, proper, and auspicious from beginning to end. However, most people these days are impatient and often do not wait until their hair turns white. They break up and go their separate ways early. Looking at the divorce cases reported in the newspaper, there is no day without them. Some divorce after being engaged but before getting married. Some divorce the morning after getting married. Some have children and still request a divorce. Adults and gentlemen want to divorce. Even poor women from Jiangbei want to divorce. The tide of divorce is becoming more urgent. More and more people are becoming vegetarians. (Divorce and leaving the meat are homophones. If you leave the meat, you are naturally a vegetarian, just kidding). Where is the vow of white heads? It is difficult to wait for the day of white hair. If this European trend continues to spread eastward and people imitate each other, I am afraid that in the future, only a few couples will be able to stay together for life and keep the "vow of white heads." Therefore, in my opinion, it is better to cancel the words "white heads" in the future, rather than having them be famous but not real. Otherwise, it would be safer to replace the word "white" with the word "black." Or it would be wonderful to change "white heads" to "Yuan heads," because "Yuan heads" are a good thing and also the price of love. When the money runs out, they will look at each other with contempt, which may not be without it. This is called "mutually agreeing to a vow of Yuan heads." But whether it is appropriate or not, please discuss it with interested people. Haha.

Brief News: Recently, a group of students from the Minli Middle School, in order to seek legitimate entertainment and regulate their spirits after class, have organized a club. When naming it, they decided to pay attention to both string and bamboo instruments and Kunqu opera. The club is located at Chongqing Lane, Fangxie Road, outside the West Gate. Students are welcome to participate enthusiastically.

Travel Notes from Southeast Asia 111

(118) By Ling·Hua·

Although commerce is said to be sluggish now, the income of Chinese people overseas and their support for their motherland are still astonishing. It is said that last month, the overseas Chinese in Fujian remitted four million yuan to Xiamen, because the shield is expensive. In the past, one shield could be exchanged for one and a half yuan, but now eighty yuan can be exchanged for one hundred yuan. Moreover, the communist rebellion in Fujian Province is very fierce. Those who have relatives and friends in Southeast Asia are flocking to Southeast Asia. Overseas is no different from the Peach Garden of Qin Dynasty.

The Burmese have also begun to use agricultural machinery, buying it from England. There are those who are trying it in various villages. It is said that the price is four thousand yuan. Yangon is the central port, with rice mills for milling rice, as well as sawmills and glass factories, but no iron factories. People say that the British are unwilling to greatly enlighten the Burmese people's knowledge, fearing that if their intelligence is high, it will be difficult to subdue them.

There are bullock carts everywhere in Myanmar. Their driving method is different from that of China. They use one bull, placing a horizontal wooden yoke on the bull's neck. Two vertical wooden pieces are then connected to the cart box, forming a cross with the horizontal yoke. It is rare to see horses. There are no donkeys in the tropics. This driving method is done by the Indian Kalas. Is it Indian style? When I read poetry, it said that six reins were in hand, which meant that in ancient times, six horses were driven. It is impossible to see this in the Jianghuai region of China. I occasionally saw someone driving six horses in Zhili. However, in Marco Polo's travelogue, there was a photo of someone driving fourteen horses during the Yuan Dynasty, which is a rare sight. The Indians of India drive elephants, and the arctic people drive deer and dogs. Now European women drive airships. Progress, progress.

The cost of living in Yangon is very high, higher than in Singapore and Penang. Originally, the currency system was calculated in rupees, which was very unsuitable, because its cost of living exceeds the value of rupees by a wide margin. Therefore, one rupee is very inadequate. For example, in Singapore, one yuan can buy one hundred points of postage stamps, while here, one rupee can only buy sixteen points. The difference is huge. However, the price of rupees is still higher than the Chinese currency. The salaries of teachers in various primary schools here are still one hundred rupees, that is, one Mongolian institution can also receive eighty or ninety rupees per month (i.e., one shield), so it is not meager compared to the poverty and desolation of China. The rupee system is the currency of India. The cost of living in India is lower than in Southeast Asia, so it is applicable in India.

In September, there was a conflict between Christianity and Buddhism for ten days. Western missionaries were in great panic. The cause was that the principals of Yangon University wanted the Burmese students to believe in Christianity, and their language was improper, which caused great misunderstanding. Hundreds of Burmese students withdrew from school and issued a declaration. The students gathered and stayed at the Great Golden Pagoda. As a result, missionaries in various places were affected. In the end, the Westerners apologized in mediation, and classes resumed. The Burmese also have the appearance of making progress day by day. They do not back down when encountering things. However, Western power in the East, as observed from various Asian countries, also has a tendency to wane when the moon is full. The policy of gunboats and commerce does not work. Religion is also difficult to win. It is thought that a third new culture will rise to replace it, which is not a theory of mutual attack between East and West. The third new culture should be responsible for reconciliation, leading the world to peace.

Warmth in the Heart 112

(3)(6)(9) By Bao·Tian·Xiao·

Chapter 17: Maintaining Youthful Looks, Emerald Ink Blurs the Eyebrows; Continuing Life Has No Way, Gold Market for Horse Bones.

Hua Laoliu had no choice. These two big packages of clothes. Entering the Shikumen (stone gate) of that pawnshop, it was as if they were buried inside, and he didn't want to redeem them anymore. Being able to pawn them for an extra dollar felt like getting an extra dollar. The meaning was to exchange the dead clothes for living money. But the appraiser in the pawnshop had already seen this, desperately killing the poor ghost. These two boxes of clothes could not even be pawned for a hundred dollars in total. Hua Laoliu had to scrape together at least two hundred dollars before he could leave. He thought that these two big packages of clothes should be able to be pawned for two hundred dollars. Even if it wasn't enough, it should be at least one hundred and fifty dollars. If he added some other things, he could get by. Now, the shop assistant came back and said that the pawnshop said it was only pawned for seventy dollars. After saying it to them again and again, and promising them that he would redeem it, many of the clothes were newly made at the tailor's shop and had not been worn a few times. In total, they were pawned for eighty dollars. Then he had to think of another way. Although he had some jewelry, he had prepared to bring it to the north to wear. When he got to Beijing, he wouldn't have any finery at all. People would say that Hua Yuanchun Laoliu must have been embarrassed in Shanghai, so he came to Beijing. Otherwise, why wouldn't he have anything? At that time, he thought of something. A guest had once given him a platinum watch, surrounded by a circle of small diamonds and a few blue diamonds. Because at that time, watches were popular for a while. That guest was an overseas Chinese from Southeast Asia, who had really spent some money on Laoliu. At this time, he heard him say that he wanted to buy a watch, and he said, "The kind of watches that are popular in the market now, twenty or thirty dollars each, are all gold-plated. After a few months, they become slippery goods. If you want to buy one, you have to buy a good one." Hua Laoliu said, "Good ones cost a lot of money." The guest said, "I'll accompany you to buy it tomorrow. You can choose it yourself." The next day, the guest accompanied him to Uliwen. A foreigner saw that there were customers coming and quickly came to greet them himself. This guest led Hua Laoliu to a large glass cabinet and said, "Choose for yourself." Laoliu looked at it and said, "Are these all silver watches?" The guest said, "There are no silver watches in this cabinet. They are all platinum." Hua Yuanchun felt a little awkward when he heard this and quickly changed his words, saying, "Aren't the prices very expensive?" The guest said, "It doesn't matter. Whichever one you like, just ask him to take it out and look at it." Hua Yuanchun chose one with small diamonds around it and a slightly rectangular shape. The guest said, "This one is very good. Try wearing it." That foreigner with a face full of beards came to help Hua Laoliu. He held Hua Laoliu's slender wrist with his hands, which were covered in yellow hair, and fastened the buckle for him. Hua Laoliu just smiled at the guest, not daring to move at all.

Yarn, Raw Cotton and Yarn Market Exhibit Firm Attitude 118

The yarn market is firm because, although the exchange rate is relaxed, the price of raw cotton on the overseas market has risen, and the local price is still high in comparison. Therefore, the bulls are still in high spirits, without any intention of relaxing. A part of the pulling force is very tight. Currently, the opposing force is very weak, so the upward trend is fierce at the slightest opportunity. Most people are looking at higher prices, reaching an extreme. However, the market price is too high, which hinders actual sales. Most prudent people are taking a wait-and-see attitude and will decide on their strategies after observing the actual sales situation next spring. The Renbiao cotton market exhibits a tight trend. Local News

Wang Zhengting Hosted the Press Circle Last Night 129

Talking About Abolishing Consular Jurisdiction

Strive to Achieve the Ultimate Goal

Foreign Minister Wang Zhengting arrived in Shanghai from Beijing at about 5:00 PM yesterday and immediately returned to his residence to rest. At 8:00 PM last night, he hosted a banquet for the Chinese and foreign press circles at the Dahua Hotel. More than 30 foreign reporters and more than 10 Chinese reporters attended. Wang was not fully recovered from his illness and did not arrive until 9:30 PM. He was received by Diao Minqian, Director of the Intelligence Department. During the banquet, Wang rose to give a speech, roughly saying that everyone still remembered that on December 28, 1929, the National Government had announced an order to abolish consular jurisdiction from January 1, 1930. At the same time, he also issued a declaration two days later to explain the National Government's order. The motive for the National Government to issue this order was, on the one hand, to reduce the causes of misunderstandings from all parties, and on the other hand, to promote the friendship between the Chinese and foreign people. The Chinese government, based on the goodwill expressed by various countries towards us in the past, firmly believed that various countries would have no objection to this principle. At the same time, the Chinese side was willing to deliberate with various countries within a considerable period of time on the measures that the government was preparing to take if any opinions were put forward. However, now that this deadline has passed, it has been twelve months, and no concrete solution has been found for the abolition of consular jurisdiction. This is something that has to be considered regrettable. According to the system of consular jurisdiction in China, it is a relic of the old era, not only is it not applicable to the modern era, but its current reality is a great obstacle to the free development of China's judicial and administrative system. The Chinese government has repeatedly explained all the ills of this system and has been repeatedly mentioned by legal experts and public opinion circles of various countries in public documents and academic discussions. Thirty years ago, several countries declared, "Once the legal situation in China and its trial methods are all proper, they will agree to give up consular jurisdiction." China has made undeniable significant progress in improving the judicial system in recent days. The National Government is really going all out to achieve it as soon as possible. The most important civil and criminal law, civil and criminal procedure law, land law, commercial law, etc., have all been modernized. Courts and prisons have also been set up throughout the country. In order to adapt to the needs of the whole country, many courts and prisons have been added in important locations. This is clear evidence of the improvement of China's judicial system. As for whether China's judicial system and judicial administration have reached the ideal standard in the minds of various countries, this is entirely a subjective view. Various countries can discuss it from their different perspectives and come to different conclusions. Therefore, this matter should be discussed fairly from the standpoint of both parties, and one side should not be biased, ignoring the other side's standpoint, just as the plaintiff should not be the judge at the same time. The investigation report of the Legal Rights Investigation Committee dispatched by the Washington Conference last time was completely one-sided observation, just like a prosecutor filing a lawsuit against a case and at the same time making a judgment on his own. Whether the judgment is fair is not known. Although this is different from the committee's report, the principle is the same. From another point of view, implementing the abolition of consular jurisdiction at this time cannot be said to be a drastic measure. There are a total of 25 countries that have treaty relations with China, of which 10 countries have no consular jurisdiction in China, 6 countries will give up in certain circumstances, and 3 countries have expired their treaties. Only 6 countries have not expired their old treaties. In other words, more than half of the treaty countries with China have their overseas Chinese citizens subject to Chinese law, and a quarter have expressed their willingness to place their overseas Chinese citizens under the protection of Chinese law. Therefore, today's abolition of consular jurisdiction only affects the people of six countries. It is especially important to note that in modern times, only China is bound by the relic of the old era, namely consular jurisdiction. Other countries that were in the same position as China in the past have long restored their judicial sovereignty. In this environment, the Chinese government and people will not vow to fight to the death to seek the early abolition of consular jurisdiction, and there is no way to face the country or themselves. The articles previously drafted by various countries, "Once the legal situation in China and its trial methods are all proper, they will agree to give up consular jurisdiction," seem to be specially designed by various countries to extend consular jurisdiction, not to abolish it. I deeply hope that the negotiations currently underway can determine the date of the official abolition of consular jurisdiction in the near future. Now the Chinese government and people have decided to make the greatest efforts to achieve this abolition goal. If the delay continues to be unresolved, it will not only be of no help, but will increase China's determination to abolish it. Therefore, I firmly believe that China will not be forced to adopt methods other than friendly negotiations to achieve this goal. Mr. Davis, a Shanghai-based reporter for the London Times, delivered a response on behalf of the guests, saying that he and his colleagues expressed great sympathy for Minister Wang's speech. China used to adhere to the closed-door policy and did not care about international affairs, but in recent years, it has made rapid progress and worked hard to govern. All facilities will be able to keep pace with the great powers. We very much hope that China's various construction plans can be realized one by one. Foreigners have great interests in China, and the abolition of consular jurisdiction must be carefully considered. The minister's political body is sick, and he came despite the snow. I and my colleagues are deeply grateful for the grand event and wish the minister a speedy recovery.
