Diplomatic Discussion Committee Submits Document to Ministry of Foreign Affairs Regarding Tap Water Issue 133

The members of the Diplomatic Discussion Committee held their 34th regular meeting at the Bank Association at No. 4 Hong Kong Road yesterday afternoon at 6:30 PM to discuss the draft proposal to the Ministry regarding the tap water issue in the Public Concession, and important cases regarding the situation of overseas Chinese in Singapore. The following is the original text of the submission to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs regarding the aftermath of the tap water issue, which has been passed: Submitted as a suggestion regarding opinions on the handling of the Shanghai Public Concession tap water issue. The committee held its 33rd regular meeting on January 9th of this year, regarding the proposal by the Director of the Office, Chen Shiguang, on the aftermath of the Shanghai Public Concession tap water price increase issue, and resolved to appoint committee members Lin Kanghou and Chu Huiseng, along with five expert committee members, Dong Xiujia, Xia Jinlin, He Dekui, Tao Leqin, and Zhang Xinglian, to conduct a detailed study. Now, according to the report, after being appointed, they immediately reviewed all the files related to the case from the Shanghai Chinese Ratepayers Association and the Shanghai Real Estate Association, and examined the accounting reports of the water company, as well as the contract signed by the Public Works Department and the British Shanghai Waterworks Company on March 17th of the 17th year of the Republic of China. After repeated joint and detailed research, it was unanimously agreed that tap water is an indispensable necessity for every resident in the concession, and its importance as a public utility is far greater than other public services such as electricity, telephone, and trams, which may have alternatives or may not be used. Moreover, since the filling of rivers and streams in the concession, residents cannot maintain their lives without using tap water. In addition, it has a close relationship with hygiene and fire prevention. Therefore, according to principles and common practice, this kind of public utility tap water can hardly achieve satisfactory results unless it is publicly operated. Now that the tap water in the Public Concession is exclusively operated by the British Shanghai Waterworks Company, and the Public Works Department has approved and signed a 20-year contract, we can only base our arguments on the established facts and seek remedial measures. The only reason for the water company's price increase this time is that the company's capital is calculated in British gold. Due to the high price of gold and the low price of silver, the Shanghai gold exchange rate has shrunk from two shillings and six pence, as stipulated in the contract, equivalent to one tael of Shanghai silver, to one shilling and six pence. As a result, the company's silver income is insufficient to distribute dividends of 9% for Class A shares, 7% for Class B shares, and 8% for Class C shares. As a result of discussions between the Public Works Department and the water company, it was approved that from September 1st of last year to December 31st of this year, regardless of whether the water price is calculated according to rent or according to water meters, all prices will be increased by 25% of the original price, that is, those calculated according to rent will be increased from 6% to 7.5%, and those calculated according to water meters will be increased from 50 cents to 62.5 cents per thousand gallons at the highest price. The reasons for the Chinese Ratepayers Association and other organizations' opposition to the price increase are: (1) The company did not reduce prices when silver was expensive and gold was cheap, so why should the company increase prices when gold is expensive and silver is cheap? (2) According to the provisions of the contract, the water price must be revised every five years, or every two years as agreed by the Public Works Department and the water company, which will expire on June 30th of this year. If the water price is to be changed, the water company must apply to the Public Works Department five months before this date. The water company did not follow this regulation when changing the water price this time, and the Public Works Department approved the price increase without delay, which is considered to be a disregard for the interests of the residents. While the dispute was ongoing, the water company used the Public Works Department's approval of the price increase as a guarantee, and openly cut off the water supply to coerce the price increase. Fortunately, after the Chinese directors strongly argued, the price increase was temporarily suspended, and the Public Works Department hired an expert to join the Public Utilities Committee to investigate all the circumstances of the water company in detail and study whether the water price could be reduced, with the aim of completing the task before September 30th of this year, so that no major accidents occurred. However, the price increase issue has temporarily come to an end, and future remedies must be planned as soon as possible. The capital of the water company is assumed to be in silver units, and its income tends to increase year by year, so the price increase would not have occurred. Moreover, the interest rate guarantee for the water company's capital is too high based on the situation in the concession and the solidity of the business. Furthermore, the water company twice issued bonus shares of 195,080 pounds in public reserve funds in the 10th and 15th years of the Republic of China, which is tantamount to making the water company's assets debts. Moreover, in the 15th year of the Republic of China, the water company unconditionally gave the assets of the tap water equipment department, valued at 200,180 taels of silver, to shareholders for independent operation. Therefore, although the main reason for the company's price increase is the high price of gold and the low price of silver, it is actually related to excessively high interest rate guarantees and the distribution of bonus shares. As a remedy, it is recommended that the authorities negotiate and order the Public Works Department to promptly revise the aforementioned contract with the water company. The main points of the revision are: (1) The water company's capital should be converted into silver units, and the calculation rate should be based on the average of the Shanghai-British exchange rate from the 9th to the 19th year of the Republic of China. (2) The original dividend rate should be limited to 6% per annum, and no bonus shares should be distributed. (3) Bonus shares may be distributed when the company has a surplus after deducting all expenses such as the original dividend rate, but the annual rate should not exceed 6% at most. If there is no dividend to be paid or the dividend paid is insufficient in the current year, no supplementary payment or compensation should be made in any subsequent year. (4) The profits from water supply outside the concession and to ships should not be separately proposed, but should be included in the total income. (5) In the future, the water price, regardless of whether it is calculated according to rent or water meter, should not exceed an average of 30 cents of silver per thousand gallons. (6) The property of the tap water equipment company should be unconditionally recovered by the water company. (7) The water company should set up more public taps for the poor to draw water. (8) The effective period of the revised contract should not exceed December 31st of the 35th year of the Republic of China at most (according to the effective period of the current contract, it will expire on December 31st of the 35th year of the Republic of China). After the expiration, the term should not be extended. Upon expiration, the Public Works Department or its successor should recover the shares of the water company at face value. Otherwise, the contract must be renegotiated. The matter concerns public utility and should be argued according to reason. The 34th regular meeting on February 12th resolved to pass the resolution and submit a document accordingly for review. We respectfully request that you grant us a negotiation, which is in the public interest. Respectfully submitted to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, with a copy of the contract attached, and a report on the review of the water company's accounts. Another letter to the Chinese directors states: Regarding the aftermath of the public concession tap water price increase issue, after discussion by our committee, it was resolved to request the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to negotiate with the Chinese directors. In addition to submitting it to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, we hereby enclose a copy of the original submission and a letter requesting you to investigate and strive for it. This is a testament to our profound friendship. Respectfully addressed to the members of the board of directors.

Business Tax Rules Meeting Yesterday 134

The Ministry of Finance Approves Zhejiang Labor Tax, Pending Revision

Letter to the City Chamber of Commerce Requesting Representatives to Strive for Four Points

The city's various trade associations previously sent representatives to Beijing to petition the Ministry of Finance to correct the business tax issue in Jiangsu and Zhejiang. The association received a reply from the Ministry of Finance yesterday, agreeing to revise the regulations separately. The association sent a letter to each representative, requesting them to strive for four points because the City Chamber of Commerce had appointed representatives to attend the discussion on business tax with the city's Finance Bureau, a matter of great importance to all industries. The contents of the letter are recorded separately as follows: "Ministry of Finance Reply" Received. The draft business tax regulations for Zhejiang Province have been approved and submitted to the Ministry by the Provincial Government. The Ministry is in the process of reviewing each item, including the business classification, tax base, and tax rate. If there are any provisions that exceed the Ministry's established guidelines and supplementary measures, they should be revised separately before replying to the Provincial Government and instructing the Finance Department to comply. Please be informed accordingly.

Letter to the City Chamber of Commerce Representatives Attending the Business Tax Discussion: Dear Gentlemen Yan Song, Qinghua, Wenqi, Jiaobo, and Songyuan, I am pleased to read in the newspaper that you have been elected by the City Chamber of Commerce to attend the discussion on the city's business tax rules. With your great talent and profound knowledge, I am deeply delighted to have you. The business tax rules are deeply and significantly related to the future interests of merchants. I believe that you have a far-sighted vision and must have a clear plan in mind, so I need not repeat myself. However, as the association has specific responsibilities, I dare to say a few words at the beginning of your appointment as a token of our support. (1) Business tax is a fundamental solution decided by the tariff reduction conference to compensate for the local tariff reduction losses. Therefore, the exact amount of tariff reduction losses in the city should first be clearly announced by the Finance Bureau to make citizens aware of it and serve as a strong basis. At the time of drafting, the tax rate should also have a certain standard. This is a consistent demand of all industries and should be strongly advocated. (2) The harm and disturbance of tariffs on merchants and people have long been criticized by the world. At this time of tax system innovation, we should strive for perfection to avoid repeating the same mistakes. For example, the tax rates set by the Jiangsu and Zhejiang provincial governments are inconsistent and are all based on goods as units, which opens the door to harassment. Our association has already detailed this in a letter sent to the Ministry of Finance of the National Government through the City Chamber of Commerce on February 7th. I believe you have already seen it in the newspapers. Therefore, when discussing the city's business tax, unless the government has other regulations below 2 per mille, the tax rate should not exceed 2 per mille. The wholesale portion should still be taxed at one-quarter. As for the collection method, it should follow the proportion method based on the business tax amount proposed by Anhui Province to avoid harassment and eliminate abuses. This should be strongly advocated. (3) There is a gap between the Chinese and foreign concessions in the city. The Chinese business community is inferior to the concessions. Although the reasons are not one-sided, the failure to implement all laws and tax rules equally is also a major cause. If the current business tax cannot be applied to stores in the concessions in the future, it will only drive away the sparrows and further nourish the prosperity of the concessions, making it even more difficult for the Chinese business community to recover. This should be strongly advocated. (4) In addition to the gap between the concessions, there are also foreign-funded commercial firms in the city. These firms often use consuls as protectors and regard our country's laws as worthless. For example, in terms of stamp tax, stores in the concessions have already affixed stamps, and there are many cases of punishment for tax evasion. However, these foreign-funded stores are uniquely spared. If the business tax rate in the future also fails to make foreign-funded stores bear equal obligations, then the cost of firms operating the same goods will invisibly increase if they are established with Chinese capital, hindering their sales. The resulting abuses will only help the economic aggression of others, making it even more impossible for Chinese businesses to gain a foothold. This should be strongly advocated. The above four points are all the most important aspects. Please take into account the special environment of the city and the difficulties of the business community, and resolutely speak for the merchants and people. Please do not be slow and complacent, and do not follow the tastes of others, lest you put the city's merchants in a situation from which they cannot recover. This is what our association sincerely prays for. I offer my sincere advice and hope for your clear understanding.

Will Send Representatives to Beijing to Petition

The Shanghai Lacework and Embroidery Trade Association recently heard that the Zhejiang Province has set the business tax rate for the industry at 20 per mille, which is extremely alarming. A special executive committee meeting will be held at 2:00 PM on the 14th (Saturday) to discuss everything, and it is planned to send representatives to Beijing to petition for exemption from business tax in order to protect the vitality of foreign trade.

Lin Kanghou's Discussion of Business Tax 136

Mr. Lin Kanghou, Chairman of the National Federation of Commerce and Co-Chairman of the Banking Branch, told a reporter from the Guowen News Agency yesterday that the business tax levied by various provinces after the tariff reduction is based on the nine guidelines formulated in the official-civilian tariff reduction conference in August of the 17th year of the Republic of China. The guidelines promulgated by the Ministry today are derived from them. There are three methods for collecting business tax: (1) according to the total amount of capital; (2) according to the total turnover; (3) according to the net profit. Each province sets its own detailed rules according to these guidelines, so they vary from province to province, which is quite noteworthy. The Spanish national treasury and people's wealth have been severely burdened by the bad business tax. The past is a lesson. I sincerely hope that the authorities in each province will be cautious about this matter. In the past, China also collected business taxes, such as the so-called "tooth posts" and licenses, but the amount collected was very small. Now, a tax of 2 per mille is not small. In the previous tariff reduction conference, the business community had already made many compromises. Now, the supplementary regulations to the guidelines promulgated by the Ministry are quite different from the principles agreed upon in the tariff reduction conference. However, the two provinces of Jiangsu and Zhejiang are levying as much as 10 per mille. A tax of 10 per mille is an inappropriate term because it should be changed to 1 percent. The guidelines agreed upon in the tariff reduction conference have completely lost their effect. What is there to say about public opinion? Now, what the business community is arguing about and sincerely requesting is only that it does not violate the guidelines of the tariff reduction conference and does not place too heavy a burden on the people. This is the general concept of the business community. I am only expressing my personal views and not representing any organization.

Issue of Implementing Factory Law in the Concession 140

It is believed that this matter has long been under consideration by your bureau, and we sincerely hope to see progress. At that time, the committee also passed a resolution, writing to the Ministry of Industry and Commerce to express its delight at the well-drafted factory regulations and hope that they will be gradually implemented and seek cooperation with foreign authorities. Subsequently, the Bureau of Industry and Commerce replied to the association on the 30th of last month, stating that it was pleased to receive the letter and that the Shanghai Women's Organizations were attentive to the improvement of social welfare and the evolution of factory conditions, which was admirable. When the Child Labor Committee was organized in 1924, China lacked a central government and there were no properly established national laws and regulations, so the bureau was unable to implement its policy of adopting Western humanitarian principles for managing the work of women and children within the scope that could be implemented in the concession. Although the autonomous improvement of factory owners and the urging of public opinion have made many achievements in improving the working conditions of women and children in the local area, the Public Works Department welcomes it very much. Municipal Defense Corps Strengthens Precautions 142

During the Business Community's Closing Period

The Shanghai Municipal Defense Corps Reorganization Committee, in view of the fact that February 14th, 15th, and 16th are the closing period for merchants, has temporarily stepped up precautions. After deciding on a plan, it was distributed to the various teams and inspection offices for reference. The plan is as follows: (1) On the 14th and 15th, each team will send out one platoon for defense. During the day, patrol teams will be organized and patrols will be conducted. From 6:00 PM to 9:00 PM, sentry posts will be deployed as appropriate in places where there is a shortage of police officers. (2) Each team should dispatch additional patrol teams as needed. (3) The time will be from 5:00 PM to 10:00 PM. (4) On the 16th, each team must send out two platoons for defense. In addition to deploying sentry posts, additional patrol teams will be dispatched. (5) The time will be from 5:00 PM to 12:00 PM. (6) The patrol teams of each team will contact the team leaders to coordinate the time for meeting patrols at any time. (7) In addition to the assigned officers and inspectors stationed on duty, the corps headquarters will also send personnel to reside in the teams to inspect the diligence of each team and the situation of the defense. (8) In the event of an emergency, they will cooperate with the military and police, but must immediately report to the corps headquarters. (9) Each team must list the number of posts deployed and submit them to the corps headquarters for the purpose of sending personnel to patrol. (10) The corps headquarters will form a patrol team of officers to patrol the various teams.

Shanghai-Ningbo Steamers Implement Escort and Increase Freight Rates 146

Agreed to Start on the 18th

Pirates are rampant on the Zhejiang sea. According to the steamers navigating the Zhejiang waters, the area around Qijiaoshan is where pirates often appear. Gunshots are often heard when steamers pass through this area. The Shanghai-Ningbo steamers have set up an escort team to prevent piracy, as reported earlier in this newspaper. The details of this case and the increase in fees are recorded separately below.

Suspension of Service Issue: Shanghai-Ningbo steamers routinely suspend service at the end of the lunar year and the beginning of the new year. This year, the central government is vigorously promoting the Gregorian calendar. The China Merchants Sanbei Ningshao and other three companies have held many meetings and decided to comply with the order and cancel the old practice of suspending service at the beginning of the lunar year. They have specifically stated this to the crew and sailors of the New Jiangtian, New Ningshao, and Ningxing steamers, and they will operate as usual. However, the British Taikoo Company's New Beijing steamer still complied with the crew's request and suspended two voyages at the beginning of the new year, which has already been decided.

Request for Weapons for Escort Police: The three companies' escort teams originally planned to board the ships on the 18th at the same time and issue航警手槍木壳槍and bullets. It was originally hoped that they would be received before that day (i.e., within this week) so that they could be issued to each ship and handed over to the escort captains and police officers stationed on the ships. However, the letter was sent to the bureau, but no reply has been received as of yesterday, and the weapons have not been received. Therefore, it may be too late to send police officers on board the ships on the 18th. If they cannot be issued this week, it may be postponed for one or two voyages. The companies have already drafted a second letter to urge the receipt of the weapons.

Details of Fee Increase: Due to the increase in航警, the fare has been increased by 20% according to the established rate. All passengers have been notified and it will be implemented on the 18th. Now that the date of implementation is near, the reporter has conducted a detailed investigation of the new freight rates and recorded the main points for public viewing.

Mrs. Lai's Views on Opium Prohibition 148

Opposing Opium Monopoly

Mrs. Lai, an American leader in drug prohibition and former director of the American delegation to the International Opium Conference, recently passed through Shanghai on her way to Fiji. It is said that during her stay in Shanghai, Mrs. Lai visited many Chinese and foreign friends and those enthusiastic about drug prohibition, discussing the issue of opium prohibition in the Far East. She paid particular attention to the current widespread talk of a foreign opium monopoly. Mrs. Lai expressed her views to Mr. Tang Shaoyi, Honorary Chairman, Mr. Wang Jingqi, Chairman, and Mr. Huang Jiahui, General Secretary, of the Chinese National Anti-Drug Association, stating that opium monopoly has been opposed by both the government and the public in China for the past ten years. The establishment of the Hague Convention in 1912 was particularly urged by those who cared about the interests of the Chinese people, and the provisions of the treaty clearly opposed the monopoly system, truly considering the interests of the Chinese people. It is incomprehensible to the world that those related to the Hague Convention are now advocating for a monopoly. Although the Hague Convention has not been fully implemented in various countries today, China is the country that benefits the most from it and should strive to promote its spirit and maintain its usefulness, and must not be the first to undermine it and abandon itself. All enemies of China's opium prohibition hope that China will implement an opium monopoly, so as to prevent the opium monopoly in colonies from becoming a target of attack by the Chinese. If important figures among the Chinese advocate for a monopoly, it would be tantamount to pleasing the enemy, making opium prohibition hopeless. Although the United States has not implemented a monopoly in Fiji, its results are better than those of other colonies that have implemented a monopoly, which shows that opium monopoly has nothing to recommend it except as a source of revenue. Mr. Tang Shaoyi, a pioneer of opium prohibition in your country, often said that advocating for the government to implement an opium monopoly is like tempting a tiger to taste human blood, which will inevitably lead to a situation where it cannot be stopped in the future. The precedent of likin [internal transit tax] can be seen. Although China is poor today, there are many ways to raise funds. Why take it from opium, like drinking poison to quench thirst? As for the Ministry of Finance hearing that it has sent people to investigate the Taiwan monopoly system, it is even more incomprehensible to outsiders. Taiwan's opium prohibition is nominally in place, but in reality, it is nothing more than a consideration for revenue. It is hoped that the Chinese National Anti-Drug Association will work hard to oppose it and prevent it from being realized. It is also hoped that the people of your country will clearly understand the pros and cons, know what to choose and what to abandon, and not cause endless trouble due to a momentary mistake.

China's Innovation: Safe Night Deposit Box 159

New Facilities at the Shanghai Bank's Avenue Joffre Branch

The safe night deposit box, originally named Night Depository, is popular in European and American banks in recent years, but has not been seen in China before. This night deposit box is made of pure steel and its style is similar to a mailbox. It is usually installed at the entrance of the bank, so as to facilitate the convenience of merchants with night market income. Every time they cannot send the money to the bank on the same day, it is inevitable that accidents will occur in the store where it is stored. With this night deposit box, all deposits after the bank's business hours can be put into the night deposit box. The method of use is extremely convenient. After obtaining the bank's permission and paying a considerable deposit, the depositor can receive a numbered money bag, a key, and a key to the night deposit box. When depositing money, they only need to put the banknotes and checks into the money bag, and the mouth of the bag is closed with a lock. No one else has a key to open the bag except the depositor. When the money bag is put into the night deposit box, there is a door on the top of the box. All depositors have a key to open this door. When the door is opened, there is a steel plate attached to the entrance of the box. At the same time, the money bag is placed on the steel plate. When the door is closed, the steel plate also falls, and the money bag falls to the bottom of the box. The box is five feet eight inches high. The advantage is that when the door is opened, there is a steel plate that can cover the entrance of the box, so no one can see or touch the contents of the box. There is another door at the bottom of the night deposit box. The next morning, the bank supervisor will open this door, take out the money bag, and wait for the depositor to come to open the bag in person. According to the ordinary deposit method, it is entered into the depositor's account. The safe night deposit box is also a new business in European and American banks in the past two or three years. It was first created in England and has not been heard of in China before. Now, the Shanghai Bank, in line with the purpose of serving society and seeking convenience for depositors, has spared no expense and specially commissioned the local Lao Jinlong Foreign Firm to order this night deposit box from the famous Helung Hall Marvin Safe Co. in the United States last year. It has been shipped to Shanghai and is now hiring craftsmen to install it at the entrance of the bank's Avenue Joffre branch. It will be completed and used soon. The night deposit box is valued at 1,600 US dollars. According to the current exchange rate, it is equivalent to more than 7,800 Chinese yuan.

Two Points That Creditors of the Riye Bank and Others Should Pay Attention To 160

Mr. Yu Qiaqing's Talk

The Guowen News Agency reported that the reporter met Mr. Yu Qiaqing yesterday and he briefly expressed his views on the Riyue Bank. Regarding the aftermath of Mr. Huang Chu Jiu, the situation is still good after Mayor Zhang and other comrades of the municipal government have properly planned and demonstrated it. Several meetings have been held in the past few days, and all comrades are pre-setting up ways to find a way out for the creditors. However, what I (Yu said himself) hope most is two points: first, the creditors' organizations should be concentrated together to form a whole organization, and never be scattered, so that both parties can easily contact each other; second, I hope that the stocks and savings receipts held by the creditors will not be transferred. It is heard that recently there have been speculators who have bought this type of bonds at extremely low prices. Once the bonds fall into their hands, crises will arise everywhere, which will lead to an unmanageable situation. Therefore, I hope that all creditors will carefully consider these two points and wait for the final benefit.

Two Major Robbers in the Huangpu Bureau Robbery Case Executed by Firing Squad 166

Two Faces of the Two Major Robbers Before Execution

One Crying Like Rain, One Smiling

Zhang Genbao and Feng Qing, well-known major robbers in the Huangpu River, and Changmao Jinsheng and Shuai Jinfu, who are at large, and others, a total of eight people, on May 30 of last year, Zhang Genbao distributed a box gun to each of them, and hired a small steamer to rob the small steamer of the Huangpu Bureau outside the Rui Rong Iron Factory in Yangshupu, killing two Chinese and foreign engineers on the spot. On June 14, Zhang Genbao, Feng Qing, and Yao Zucheng, who received the stolen goods, were arrested by the water patrol police and sent to the local court. Zhang Genbao directly confessed that the foreign engineer shot him, and the bullet grazed his waist, so he returned the shot and killed the foreign engineer. The Chinese engineer was killed by Changmao Jinsheng. Yao Zucheng claimed that his wife was giving birth at home and he accidentally boarded the stolen ship. The prosecutor filed a public prosecution in accordance with the Law on Punishing Bandits and sentenced Zhang Genbao and Feng Qing to death and Yao Zucheng to two years of imprisonment. The case was immediately submitted to the Provincial Government for review and should be executed by firing squad. Yesterday, the court was ordered to execute the sentence. At noon, the court sent a confidential letter to Chief Prosecutor Liu of the Prosecutor's Office, who appointed the original handler, Prosecutor Yang Qi, as the execution supervisor. Because Zhang was a well-known bandit leader, he was supervised by police officer Chen Xihui, who added ten execution police officers, Wang Jianqing, Gu Hanqing, Xu Guoguang, Zou Zhendong, Zhang Chunsen, Zhu Baochang, Jiang Huanzhang, Cao Ziqian, Cai Zuoqing, and Zhang Cheng, all fully armed. At 2:00 p.m., they went to the detention center to take out the two criminals, Zhang Genbao and Feng Qing, and bound them according to the law. When they were escorted onto the car, Feng Qing's wife was coming to visit. When she saw this situation, she burst into tears, which was very miserable. The police officers then pushed the two criminals onto the car and drove quickly to the Second Prison in Caohejing. At this time, He Dafu, the head of the water patrol police, also went to the scene with Bao Tan Ge Changsheng to watch the execution. Prosecutor Yang immediately took the seat with Warden Dong Changmin and Secretary Li Ting. When asked, Feng Qing confessed that he was 29 years old, from Pudong, and had been a boat rocker. He lived at No. 75 Shanhoushan, Xinhui. He requested to write a letter to the Shunxing Pavilion in Shanhoushan, Xinhui, to hand it over to his father-in-law, Chen Wengui, to collect the body and asked to take care of his children. His wife was still young, and he told her to recruit a man to take care of her and asked his two sisters to take care of her. After saying this, tears fell like rain. His attachment to his family was very miserable. A person who is about to die speaks well. Later, Zhang Genbao was brought up for questioning. He was 24 years old, from Pudong. He asked to send a letter to the Wanshengtai shoe store in Zhongshi, Yangjiadu, to hand it over to his maternal uncle, Xu Xisheng, and to ask his new sister-in-law to pay 450 yuan and ask Mr. Zhu and Lawyer Zhou to return 160 yuan. The 450 yuan was for his family to use, and the 160 yuan was to compensate his maternal uncle's losses. He did not want to collect his body. The money for collecting the body was better used at home. When a person dies, he is mashed into meat sauce and does not know anything. Why bother to bury him? Death is death anyway, but our death is a little ugly. Please shoot us immediately. He also said that he and Sheng Genbao, who had been executed by the headquarters, were brothers. He had kidnapped a Chen family and got more than 100,000 yuan. He never robbed less than a thousand yuan. He usually spent money lavishly. He had been a thief more than once and should have died long ago. But this time he did not rob much and was really fooled by Changmao Jinsheng. His attitude of defying the law was not changed until his death, and his smiling expression was unchanged. The judge then ordered the execution. Chen directed the police to take him down for execution by firing squad. After the inspectors inspected the bodies, they were taken away for burial.

Continuous Rain and Snow 167

Merchants Complain About Collecting Debts

Wusong Power Lines Suddenly Broken

At about 9:00 p.m. the night before (the 11th), it suddenly snowed in Shanghai, with snowflakes as large as goose palms. It seemed that it would not stop soon, but it cleared in less than 20 minutes. At midnight, six-petaled flowers fell again, and Shanghai became a jade world. Yesterday the weather was gloomy, and the rain master and the wind god came one after another. The rain was even heavier at night, the roads were muddy and difficult to walk, and pedestrians complained. At the end of the lunar year, merchants are accustomed to collecting debts everywhere, but they all sighed in despair when they saw this situation. Also, at about 10:00 p.m. the night before, it snowed heavily in Wusong. The wooden power poles, initially crushed by the snow, were broken by the wind. It is estimated that dozens of poles were broken on Fort Taiwan, Baoshan County Road, Taixing Road, and Tongji Road. Therefore, the phones in Songbao and Tongji were not working yesterday. Dai Zhongqiu, the manager of the Songyang Telephone Company, personally led the mechanics to inspect the roads and immediately hired workers to repair them in order to facilitate traffic. It will take about three or four days to fully restore the lines. Also, the snow in the Pudong area was no less than six or seven inches thick. The farmland and roads were all white, and the jade buildings and pavilions became a silver world. The roads with frequent travelers were still covered with snow in the morning, and people could walk on them. However, in the afternoon, the weather warmed up and gradually melted, and the main roads showed signs of mud.

Eight Cases of Kidnapping by Bandit Leader Wang Zhixiang 168

Four Cases Did Not Occur in the Public Concession

Wang Committed Too Many Crimes to Remember

Shu Xiaogou, a resident of Gaoxie Ao, Zhoushan, Dinghai County, Zhejiang Province, was kidnapped on the ninth day of the eleventh month of the lunar calendar. The bandits wrote to his family, intending to demand 10,000 yuan. The negotiation location was with Chinese Detective Wang Changgen and undercover detectives Wang Yingjie and Yan Ji of the Zha Old Gate Police Station in Shanghai. Yu Jinfang, Ni Ronggao, Wang Zhixiang (also known as Wang Biezui and Wang Haixiang), Cao Tongyu, Zou Jierui, Xia Zicheng, Zhao Ayu, Cao Xingzhang, and other eight bandits from Ningbo were arrested at the Lao Ding Sheng Hotel and Lingnan Hotel and sent to the Special District Court. Ni Ronggao confessed that Shu Xiaogou had been beaten to death inside a coffin near the Land God Temple in Xujia Village, Zhoushan, after being kidnapped. Wang Zhixiang confessed that he was the leader of the gang and had committed eight kidnapping cases, including the kidnapping of Bei Runsheng. The court ordered a postponement and ordered an investigation into Shu's body. It is now known that Shu was indeed killed, with one gunshot wound to each of his head, heart, and waist. The body has been inspected by Dinghai County, and the family has been ordered to claim the body. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Zhou Hanting of the Special Court continued the trial in a criminal court. The police station's lawyer, Ru Baoyi, stated that, excluding Yu Jinfang and Ni Ronggao, whose crime of kidnapping Shu took place in the interior, Wang Zhixiang, although he was aware of this case, had committed four kidnapping cases in the concession. Wang had previously confessed to eight cases, but the other four cases were not prosecuted because they did not occur in the Public Concession. As for the remaining five defendants, the police station found no evidence and originally intended to withdraw the charges. However, according to the Criminal Procedure Law, a defendant who has been publicly prosecuted cannot have the charges withdrawn. It is also unknown whether Dinghai County needs to transfer the five defendants, so they are temporarily detained at the police station. Today, only Wang Zhixiang was brought to court regarding the cases of kidnapping Shi Jiufeng, Liang Huibao, Wu Fangpu, and Wu Songyan. He will now present each case individually for questioning. The first case is the kidnapping of Shi Jiufeng. On the morning of February 24, 1928, at 9:00 AM, Shi was kidnapped by bandits about 200 yards away from his home at 237 Xinji Bang Road and taken to 19 East Yokohama Road. Later, the Jing'an Temple Police Station cracked the case, and the bandits opened fire and resisted arrest. The police returned fire, killing three bandits and injuring one West Deputy Police Chief. Two bandits, Wang Wenhui and Zhou Yuesheng, were captured. According to their confessions, a person named Wang was the leader. The police then showed them photos of all suspects and photos of previous offenders borrowed from the French Police Station. The two identified Wang Zhixiang's photo from the French Police Station, saying that he was the person named Wang. This can be testified to by West Police Chief Gellerber. Wang has also confessed to this. The second case is Liang Huibao, who was kidnapped on Peng Road on December 6, 1927. When the car reached Laobaizi Road, Liang shouted for help and was shot to death by the bandits. In this case, the police arrested Ma Guisheng, Zhu Xiaomao, and Zhang Binglin, all of whom confessed to Wang Zhixiang's involvement. The third case is Wu Fangpu, the compradore of Mitsui & Co., who was kidnapped on Tibet Road on October 25, 1928, and held at 409 Minhou Lane, Hartung Road, for about five days. The bandits moved Wu, who was guarded by a bandit who walked and did not ride in a car. When Wu saw the police, he shouted wildly. The police arrested a bandit named Zhou Ziyun, and Wu was rescued. Zhou confessed that Wang Zhixiang was involved. The fourth case is Wu Songyan, the owner of Da Lun Silk Factory, who was kidnapped at the intersection of Qipu Road and North Fujian Road on September 6, 1928, and later ransomed for 70,000 yuan. Wang Zhixiang received 11,500 yuan. Wu did not report the case to the police station, so the details are unknown. Then, Wang Zhixiang's confession was presented to the court. Shi Jiufeng, a Ningbo native who works in hardware, testified that he did not know Wang Zhixiang and described the kidnapping. Liang Huibao's son, lawyer Liang Yuming, submitted evidence, but since he was not present at the scene, he could not provide proof. Wu Fangpu, 54 years old, from Hangzhou, testified that the bandits moved him due to internal strife. He had never seen Wang Zhixiang. Wu Songyan did not appear. Lawyer Yan Luqi appeared on his behalf and stated that Wu had gone to his hometown of Huzhou for business and could not attend the court. He presented Wu's letter as evidence. Wang Zhixiang was questioned and confessed to receiving 11,500 yuan in the Wu Songyan case. Although he admitted to the cases, he attributed them all to others. Judge Zhou Han questioned him about the case details and his accomplices, but Wang claimed that his mind was unclear and he did not remember anything. He stated that the confession presented by the police station was indeed written by him and contained no errors. He asked the court to convict him based on the confession and not to question him further. Judge Zhou reviewed the confession and ordered a postponement for further investigation, as the case still required investigation.

Husband, Wife, and Daughter All Perish Together

The Truth About the Wang Zhigao Property Dispute 173

The recent report about Wang Zhigao suing Wang Zhixue and Wang Zhenhuan, owners of Wang Yutai Tea House, for ancestral property was based on the plaintiff Wang Zhigao's complaint. Here is a more detailed account of the case based on inquiries from various parties:

Wang Xianyong of Jixi had three sons: Lizheng (the eldest), Lihuan (the second), and Lizhu (the third). In the early years of the Xianfeng era, Xianyong divided his self-acquired fields and houses among the three sons according to their families, each pursuing their own business. Three copies of the property division documents were created as proof. After the division, Lihuan and Lizhu stayed home to farm and study, while Lizheng went out to trade. He first came to Shanghai as an apprentice in a store. After many years of hard work, he saved over a hundred yuan and established Wang Yutai Tea House in Nanshi, which is the foundation of today's tea house. This was an independent business created by Lizheng after the property division. In Jixi, after Lizheng left, the area was affected by war within a few years. Lihuan died in the disaster, and the properties and division documents of each branch were burned. Lizheng, however, always supported the lives of his brothers in his hometown. In the 25th year of Guangxu, Lizheng's eldest son, Zhixue (the defendant in this case), Lihuan's adopted son, Zhigao (the plaintiff in this case), and Lizhu's son, Zhijing, wrote three copies of a document stating that the ancestral property had already been divided and re-established the division agreement, with each signing their names. Ten relatives, clan chiefs, and intermediaries also signed as witnesses. The facts were clear, and there was no dispute for more than thirty years. Unexpectedly, seeing Wang Yutai Tea House prospering, Wang Zhigao suddenly sued for ancestral property in the French Concession Public Court in May 1929, using similar language as in the current complaint. Wang Pinxue refuted the allegations with factual evidence. Zhigao, knowing he could not win, requested mediation. Zhixue agreed out of clan affection. Zhigao then wrote a document withdrawing the lawsuit, personally signing his name, with witnesses Hu Shi and the lawyers Wang Tingjie, Lu Shaozong, Yao Zhaodi, and Qin Liankui signing as witnesses. The full text of the document is recorded below:

Withdrawal of Lawsuit Declaration by Wang Zhigao: Regarding Wang Zhigao's ancestor, Xianyong, who had three sons, Lizheng (the eldest), Lihuan (the second), and Lizhu (the third), all the ancestral property was inherited by the three branches in the early years of the Xianfeng era. Due to the chaos of the times, the property division documents were lost. Therefore, in the 25th year of the Guangxu era, Zhixue (the eldest son), Zhigao (the second son, i.e., myself), and Zhijing (the third son) re-established a document with the help of relatives, clan chiefs, and intermediaries, explaining the previous situation. Because Zhigao is the adopted son of Lihuan, he received ten mu of fields and a plot of land from Zhixue, which was also documented by relatives and intermediaries. Both documents were signed by Zhigao, Zhixue, and Zhijing. Most of the relatives who signed are now deceased, but the relatives Shan Yu and the intermediary Cheng Shangtian are still alive. Once verified, the truth will be clear. However, Zhigao's situation is dire, unlike Zhixue and Zhijing, who can support themselves. Last year, he entrusted lawyer Wang Tingjie to send a letter to Zhixue, ostensibly requesting property division but actually hoping to receive some assistance. Zhixue, misunderstanding Zhigao's intention, firmly refused, entrusting lawyer Qin Liankui to reply. Zhigao, in a moment of anger, hastily filed a lawsuit in the French Concession Mixed Court, claiming that the Wang Yutai Tea House, operated solely by Lizheng's branch, was common property, and requesting the seizure of properties in Hangzhou and Shanghai, almost completely severing brotherly ties. Fortunately, while preparing the lawsuit, Zhigao informed his lawyer of the long-analyzed real situation. Under the lawyer's guidance, he voluntarily reconciled. He immediately went to Zhixue, declaring his error and requesting no counter-suit. He obtained Zhixue's understanding, who, mindful of Zhigao's sincerity and repentance, treated him generously, promising not to pursue previous debts and providing funds for his return home. On the day of signing, through the certifying lawyer, the funds were paid in full. Zhigao, having realized his error, vowed to reform. In addition to submitting a statement withdrawing the lawsuit and promising no further disputes, he specifically wrote a personal declaration withdrawing the lawsuit, which was handed over to Zhixue for safekeeping. If he ever again contemplates receiving property from other branches, he agrees to be gathered by the clan and removed from the family genealogy, no longer considered a descendant of the Wang family. This document was submitted by Zhigao to the French Concession Public Court for record and the lawsuit was withdrawn. Therefore, the Wang Zhigao property dispute was legally resolved and settled. Unexpectedly, Zhigao, in October of last year, invited his brother Zhijing to sue Zhixue and his son Zhenhuan in the French Public Court, requesting the division of ancestral property. Zhixue and others hired lawyer Shen Junru to argue in court. Subsequently, the French Public Court, on December 22, ruled to reject the plaintiff Wang Zhigao's lawsuit. The ruling stated, "In the case of Wang Zhigao and Wang Zhijing, the plaintiffs, and Wang Zhixue and Wang Zhenhuan, the defendants, regarding the dispute over the division of ancestral property, after questioning both parties, the defendant submitted a reconciliation document dated August 1, 1929, and requested the rejection of the plaintiff's lawsuit. This court has instructed to await a ruling on file. Upon investigation of the reconciliation document, there is no fixed form or requirement for signatures from both parties. Since the document has been filed with this court, it should be considered valid. The plaintiff's lawsuit cannot be established. However, the second plaintiff, Wang Zhijing, is not listed in the document and can file a separate lawsuit. This court will schedule a separate hearing to begin the debate. Furthermore, according to the plaintiff's request to withdraw the lawsuit on December 9 of this year, this court originally intended to settle the matter peacefully, and the defendant has not filed a counterclaim. Therefore, the plaintiff's request should be approved. This is the ruling." This shows that the matter has indeed been legally resolved. However, Wang Zhigao continues to litigate, filing a lawsuit in the Special District Court this January regarding the same incident. The court heard the case on the 5th of this month in the Ninth Court. The defendant hired lawyer Zhang Yaozeng to represent him in court. Lawyer Zhang argued that the subject matter of the lawsuit had already been reconciled, and the defendants' residences were not in the Public Concession. The case involved the division of ancestral property and was not related to the business operations of Wang Yutai Tea House. Therefore, it was inappropriate to base jurisdiction on a business establishment in the Public Concession. He immediately requested the court to dismiss the plaintiff's lawsuit to avoid unnecessary litigation. The court ordered that the matter be heard and ruled upon. It is reported that the Special District Court declared its ruling yesterday, dismissing the plaintiff Wang Zhigao's lawsuit.

Truly Daring

Yu Debiao, a 21-year-old man from Haiyan, was originally from a good family and had worked in a sauce garden, possessing a membership card from the Soy Sauce Industry Association. Due to his fondness for extravagance, he lived alone in the Zhongxing Inn. Every day, he would go to various shops or business places under the pretext of soliciting business, stealing items. Jiang Youzhi's Letter to the French Public Court 175

The Xinsheng Society reports that the divorce case between lawyer Dong Yu and his wife has been heard several times by the French Public Court without a result. It is reported that Jiang Youzhi sent another letter to the French Public Court yesterday, detailing the circumstances of being forced to sign the divorce papers and requesting a fair judgment. The letter states: Regarding the divorce case between the defendant Jiang and the plaintiff Dong Jingxi (Dong Yu), the court has heard the case multiple times. The incident of being forced to sign at the New World Hotel provides a crucial reference for this case. Please present this to the judge. Since being ostracized by the plaintiff, the defendant has been borrowing accommodation from Dong Kang. Dong Kang, because of the defendant's poor judgment in choosing a spouse, bears lifelong regret. He is sympathetic and treats her as one of his daughters, so she calls him adoptive father. Last year, when Mr. Lu passed away, the plaintiff told the adoptive father that he wanted to divorce the defendant. The adoptive father strongly disapproved, urging them to reconcile. Unexpectedly, the plaintiff did not listen, leading to this lawsuit. The adoptive father repeatedly called the plaintiff to his home, reasoning with him to withdraw the lawsuit and consider a separation. However, the plaintiff was confused, believing that someone was hindering the matter and making threatening remarks. On the first of this month, the adoptive father went to the communication office jointly operated by Wang Lianghou and Fan Songji on Aiduya Road. Lawyer Wang said that Fan Songji, who has a sworn brotherhood with the plaintiff, was willing to negotiate the matter. The adoptive father also met with Fan while investigating other matters. Fan Songji said that reconciliation was currently difficult. If they could stick to the agreement, they might be able to reconcile in the future. He suggested temporarily separating with 3,000 yuan and a reasonable allowance for the education of the young daughter. He was willing to act as a mediator. The adoptive father agreed to convey the message and stated that he would only agree after the cousin Dong Banggan returned to Shanghai to discuss the guardianship conditions. On the second, lawyer Wang summoned the defendant to the communication office to meet Fan Songji. Although the defendant was pressured by the consensus, she did not fully agree. At 9:00 PM on the third afternoon, the adoptive father received an invitation from Fan and Wang from the New World Hotel. The adoptive father accompanied the defendant to room 239 to talk, assuming that they were discussing conditions to avoid rumors. He asked the adoptive mother, Ms. Chi, to accompany the defendant. It was heard that the plaintiff was also in the next room. At that time, there were many men and women who inquired about the situation. Some expressed outrage, while others offered gentle persuasion. Fan Songji conveyed the plaintiff's words and asked lawyer Wang to draft a divorce agreement, and lawyer Zhan Jifeng was invited to the scene to witness. The divorce agreement was purchased and they were asked to sign it that night. At this time, the defendant was extremely troubled, and the situation remained unresolved for three hours. After the adoptive father telegraphed the situation, he first spoke with lawyer Zhan, requesting that he inform them how to arrange the matter after the divorce and that all considerations must be taken into account. The speaker asserted that they had no legal right to speak, because the speaker was not legally authorized to assert anything. The speaker insisted on waiting for the cousin to return to Shanghai before deciding. Immediately, the speaker accompanied the defendant and others to return. On the fourth, they were summoned by the court. The plaintiff asserted four points: (1) Because the adoptive father entrusted the former agent lawyer Sheng Shengxi to express the situation of forced signing, he said that witnesses did not have the law of entrusting a lawyer to represent them, and refused to speak. (2) He said that indefinite postponement was the custom of the court, and the lawyer could not know, and criticized Wang's lawyer for lack of experience. (3) He said that after the divorce, the defendant was separated from the Dong family and listened to her survival, without the need for the head of the family to seek protection. (4) Chen pointed out the contract drafted by lawyer Wang, pointing to the acquiescence to this matter. The speaker purely manipulated it. The speaker investigated the first and second points as legal issues that the defendant did not know. The third point was that the plaintiff indulged in sound and color, lacking the morality of husband and wife, treating the defendant far less than a maid. Once abandoned, it would be possible to let her drift. In the case of the defendant, the shame of being cast down would be engraved in her mind and the life would still have to be maintained by the husband and mother's family. In addition, the young daughter Yan Sheng was only eight years old. It was the blood of the Dong family. How could the mother's family sever relations together? The fourth point certainly alluded to the adoptive father. The adoptive father's sincere persuasion was his original intention. If he was said to have manipulated it, it was a pseudonym for waiting for a good price, with the words of contempt for a person who had been cultivated and claimed to be obedient to his elders. Although the name was not explicitly mentioned, the speaker was spared criminal liability, and the speaker's conscience was not to be desired. The above points, if there are public opinions, there is no need to sort them out. The court should hear that the plaintiff is slightly familiar with poetry and etiquette and is ashamed to accept this condition. Reviewing the plaintiff's first statement, the divorce was based on the defendant's illness of pulmonary disease. Whether pulmonary disease is a condition for divorce and whether the defendant had pulmonary disease should still be judged by the court according to law, which is true convenience. Respectfully to the French Public Court of the Shanghai French Concession.

Impersonating a Detective to Swindle 176

Falsely Claiming a Nephew of Mao Jingen is Getting Married

Sending Out Five to Six Hundred Invitations

Recently, new scams have emerged in Shanghai. Someone even impersonated a detective to swindle money from various places. It has been reported that someone impersonated Zhang Ziying, a detective of the French Police Station, and defrauded 500 yuan from a customs broker. It has now been learned that a rogue recently impersonated Mao Jingen, a detective of the special agency of the French Police Station, and sent out invitations (commonly known as "striking autumn wind"), falsely claiming that Mao Tank's nephew, Mao Kaixiang, would be married on February 11 of the solar calendar, which is December 24 of the lunar calendar. His home was said to be at 10 Xinmin Lane, Arber Road, and the banquet was to be held at Fuxingyuan Restaurant, Pingwang Street, Wuma Road. A total of five to six hundred invitations were sent. Detective Mao learned of the matter and, considering the perpetrators' audacity, reported it to the police chief. He also went to 10 Xinmin Lane and Fuxingyuan Restaurant to arrest them, but the perpetrators had already fled. Detective Mao reported back to the police chief, who ordered him to arrest them for investigation.

Robbers Send Gifts to Get the Door Opened 177

Aunt Hu Reports to the Police and Deters the Robbers

Female Robber Throws Away Items and Flees

Hu Baoli, from Anhui, engages in the bamboo and wood business and is very wealthy. He built his own house at 23 Santaidock, Nanshi. The house is quite spacious and richly decorated, attracting the attention of bandits. The day before yesterday, Hu's aunt suddenly heard urgent knocking on the door. She opened the door and saw a beautiful woman wearing a black cloak and high-heeled leather shoes, dressed fashionably. She was carrying a basket of tangerines and two boxes of dry snacks, claiming that they were gifts sent by the Chen family. Upon hearing that they were gifts, Hu's aunt ordered someone to open the door and welcome her in. However, upon closer inspection, she found the woman's face unfamiliar. As she was about to inquire about the details, two unexpected guests suddenly broke in, immediately drawing handguns from their pockets, warning her not to make a sound. At this point, Hu's aunt realized she had encountered robbers. She quickly shook her head at the two robbers, signaling them not to shoot, and said, "What do you want? Just take whatever you need." As she spoke, she stepped back and quickly closed the door to the side room, then escaped out the back door. She used the telephone to notify the district's police station. After receiving the report, the station chief, along with Inspector Sun and Police Chief Liu, rushed to the scene to encircle and arrest the robbers. At that time, the robbers saw that Hu's aunt had escaped and realized that the situation was unfavorable. They immediately turned around and fled. The woman who had knocked on the door with the gifts also quickly discarded the items she was carrying and fled with the two robbers towards the Bund. The police team failed to capture them, so they took the gifts abandoned by the woman back to the station. Yesterday, they prepared a document to report to Director Chen of the Municipal Public Security Bureau for instructions.

Detective Stabbed by Bandits 178

Three Criminals Have Been Arrested

The western suburbs of Shanghai are remote, and it is dangerous for pedestrians at night. The Putuo Road Police Station dispatches detectives every night to patrol the area for protection. On the night of the fourth of this month, Detective Yuan Xinzhong was patrolling the entrance of a lane on Lubansheng Road when he saw a suspicious person. He immediately arrested him. Unexpectedly, two accomplices suddenly came out of the lane. One of them stabbed Yuan in the face and abdomen with a knife, causing him to be wounded and bleeding. The arrested bandit was rescued. Yuan, wounded, hired a car to report to the police station. The police chief ordered him to go to the hospital for treatment and instructed the detectives to strictly investigate and arrest the criminals for punishment. The night before last, Detective Zhao Fuhai arrested a criminal named Lou Jinbao from Shandong Province at the intersection of Xiaoshadu Road and Lubansheng Road. He also went to a thatched house at 150 Xiaoshadu Road and found the knife used to stab Yuan, a flashlight, and fourteen pawn tickets. Upon questioning, he learned that an accomplice named Wang Shunhe was hiding at 123 Sanguantang Street, Nanshi. He immediately coordinated with the police station to arrest Wang. Soon after, the police station arrested Xu Guangfa in Shiba Jian, Pudong, who was also involved in the Yuan stabbing case. Currently, except for Xu, who is temporarily detained by the Public Security Bureau, Lou and Wang were sent to the Special District Court yesterday morning for investigation. However, Detective Yuan is still receiving treatment in the hospital, and Xu has not been formally charged. Therefore, police station lawyer Wang Yaotang requested a postponement. After Judge Cheng conducted a preliminary trial, he ordered them to be detained for further investigation.

Letters to the Editor

Dear Editor, Yesterday, your newspaper's local news column mentioned that Tongyang steamships were also suspended, which is inconsistent with the facts. After checking, the inland river steamship bureaus affiliated with our association had already resolved in the executive committee meeting to strictly abide by the orders of the central and municipal party and government agencies and observe the national calendar and abolish the lunar New Year's Day, generally without suspending navigation. A notice was issued to all steamship bureaus to comply. Therefore, all bureaus operated as usual, and there was no suspension of navigation. However, a few cargo steamship bureaus use the availability of goods as the standard. They operate when there are goods and stop when there are no goods, so there is no fixed schedule. Even if one or two bureaus do not operate, it is not related to the abolition of the lunar New Year's Day. This letter is to inform you, hoping for correction. Sincerely, Shanghai Inland River Steamship Bureau Association, February 12, 20

Book Review

The Ethnic Groups of the Southern Wilderness 181

By Wei Juezhong, Man Yin

Everyone knows that we are now in the era of the 20th century, an era of civilization and evolution, from the Stone Age and Iron Age to the age of machines. In this era, human social organization has also changed from primitive communist society and feudal society to industrial society. In the metropolises of Europe, America, Japan, and China, we see skyscrapers, prosperous and splendid streets, cars, trams, dance halls, and playgrounds, all of which are extravagant and cater to people's use and entertainment, demonstrating the capabilities of material progress to the fullest. In the countryside, especially in the countryside of our China, which is known as an ancient country, drastic changes are now also obviously taking place, a change that is different from the old, simple past. Whether in politics or economics, as long as I pay attention, I can feel it.

In short, in modern society, whether in the city or in the countryside, in Europe and America or in East Asia, almost the entire globe makes us feel that human society has undergone many changes, changes from the embryo of the old society to the form of the new society. Only slowly did we have today. Undoubtedly, this change is the progress of human culture and the development of social systems. Therefore, it is difficult for us to believe that there are still uncivilized humans and undeveloped societies like our ancestors thousands of years ago on this same earth and in the same era.

However, friends, let's take a look at this book, "The Ethnic Groups of the Southern Wilderness," written by Wei Juezhong. Compare the life of the natives of Southeast Asia recorded in this book with what we call civilized humans. What feelings should arise?

Mr. Wei is a traveler who has ambitions to travel the world. He has been drifting in the south for seven years. Therefore, this book not only makes him feel that "what is described in the book is based on what the author has personally heard and seen, and I am confident that it is different from those who have never set foot in Southeast Asia but talk about it lavishly," but also makes us readers never feel that someone is making up stories and lying to us. The entire book is divided into two volumes. The first volume describes the life of the savage Gaya people of Dutch New Guinea, and the second volume describes the Wata ethnic group between the east coast of Sumatra and Tapannuli. Each volume contains many short stories that can be separated independently. This is probably what the author wrote down while traveling in a hurry. We don't have to be "nitpicking" and blame him for not organizing it into systematic chapters. In fact, this is the only way to truly preserve the travelogue style and interest that combines narrative and commentary.

In the first three chapters of the first volume, we are told about the happy life of the Gaya people, who sing and dance every day, the topography of Gaya and the country to which it belongs, and the origin of its name. Then, it unfolds to the strange customs of the Gaya people, such as the Gaya woman's ideal lover, who is not beautiful, rich, or has a position, but a hero who has killed many people. For the Gaya people's wedding, the bride must first give offerings to relatives and friends, and on the second day, she must also be enjoyed by the elderly and elders in the neighborhood. Two or three days before the wedding, the groom invites two relatives and friends to take the bride as a test product. Aren't these all things that we consider strange?

There are also many other habits that we have never heard of, like primitive aborigines, such as those described in the chapters "Life and Death," "The Gaya People's Mathematics," "A Good Skill," "The Sky as a Tent and the Earth as a Seat," "Natural Disasters," and "Anarchy." Due to space limitations, I won't go into detail.

The second volume describes the Wata people, just like the first volume. However, in fact, the living habits of the Wata people are very different from those of the Gaya people. For example, the Gaya people can share their wives, while the Wata people absolutely do not allow it. Unmarried women of the Wata people can flirt with any man (those with the same surname are not included), while the Gaya people cannot. The Wata people have surnames and know how to grow rice and store it, while the Gaya people cannot do any of these. In the chapter "Practitioners of Free Love," the love life of Wata girls is described, which is quite strange to us, because in most places in human sexual life, men are active and women are passive, but Wata girls are not.

Looking at the Wata ethnic group described in the second volume as a whole, it is much more evolved than the Gaya people in the first volume, because the former seems to have reached the period of hunting, animal husbandry, and cultivation, while the latter is still stuck in the period when primitive people only know how to collect animals and plants from nature for a living. However, compared with us Eurasian people, who have progressed to the era of using machines, what will it be like? At present, on the same earth, some humans have evolved to the era of fire wheels, airplanes, and almost electricity, while other humans are still stuck in the life of primitive people. Mr. Wei now takes the customs and habits of that part of humanity that is still stuck in the life of primitive people and writes them into a book. As Mr. Zheng Hongnian, who wrote the preface to this book, said, "It is enough to provide materials for the study of anthropology and folklore for scholars around the world." Mr. Liu Shimu said, "How can the benefits to scholars who study society be shallow?"

On the other hand, this book's record of the abuse and downfall of overseas Chinese in Southeast Asia also greatly stimulates our readers' national consciousness. Although the author does not have a special chapter on this, it can be seen between the lines:

"......Dutch officials forbid overseas Chinese from carrying coconuts......"

Page 74

"......Any Chinese who marries a Gaya woman will be forced to divorce, and the children born will also be forced to be given to the aborigines......" Page 75

"......After the European War, the Dutch imposed a so-called (30%) war tax in their territory......As a result, countless overseas Chinese went bankrupt." Same page

"In various places in the Dutch colony, opium is sold publicly by the government, and 90% of opium smokers are our overseas Chinese, spending tens of millions of guilders every year." Page 76

"As many of our compatriots are missing in Southeast Asia as there are sands in the Ganges River, but has anyone ever investigated?" Volume 2, page 4

What a painful cry! The description of the difficulties in trading between overseas Chinese and aborigines in the article "Servants of the Savages" (page 69) is really pitiful.

In recent years, our government has gradually paid attention to overseas Chinese in Southeast Asia, and many people have aspired to study Southeast Asia and travel to Southeast Asia. Several books on Southeast Asia have also been published in the market. However, I have not seen a book as rich in materials and detailed in records as this book. So, this book can also serve as a reference book for studying Southeast Asian culture.

The author's writing is lively, the sentences are fresh, the narration is concise, and the tone is fluent. There are several ancient poems and many pictures scattered throughout the book. So, this book can also be read as a story novel. I heard that Mr. Wei is still working on the third, fourth, and so on volumes of records about his travels, and he is preparing to depart to the Northeast, travel across the country and around the world soon. Here, we sincerely wish him success.
