The Art World

The Implementation of Aesthetic Education 182

By Tang Jun

The words "Aesthetic Education" seem to be frequently found in the eyes and writings of Chinese people. The general public seems to attach considerable importance to it. However, where are the achievements of the implementation of aesthetic education? What effects has it had on the public and artists? Whenever we think of these two questions, we will always regret the long delay in developing this great avenue of aesthetic education.

The author is here to discuss "Aesthetic Education" with everyone, not only hoping that readers will express a considerable or enthusiastic sympathy for what I have said, but also hoping that you will expand your sympathy and launch a powerful movement for the implementation of aesthetic education.

"Aesthetic Education" has two meanings: (1) To the public: to popularize art, socialize art, and make art appreciative. In general terms, it is to beautify life and beautify society. (2) To artists: to specialize art and create art. In general terms, it is called "Art Education." The first point is to cultivate a general "aesthetic consciousness" and artistic "appreciation ability" among the public. The second point is to cultivate a general "aesthetic consciousness" and specialized artistic "creation ability" among artists. The so-called "Aesthetic Education" includes these two meanings. This is only when viewed from the receiving end that there is a distinction between "the public" and "artists." But when viewed from the launching end, it is a unified whole.

When we implement aesthetic education for the public, it is not to make every member of the public an artist, but to enable the general public to have the ability and interest to appreciate art, and to instill a kind of "aesthetic consciousness" in the general society. General life must be immersed in a kind of "aesthetic consciousness." Whether it is a public group or a personal residence, social customs, or personal behavior, they should all be shrouded in a kind of "aesthetic atmosphere." In other words, it is to make society artistic and life aesthetic.

When we implement aesthetic education for artists, it is not to use the same model to print them into a uniform appearance, nor is it to hold the same rules of implementation and let them embark on the same road. It is to lead the great souls of artists into the great realm of true art, to present the broad elements needed by artists broadly in front of the artists, so that their inner extension and outer package, psychology and physiology, are influenced and transformed by these environments and materials. Their minds will conceive a beautiful idea, and their eyes and hands will naturally form a great skill. The fusion of this beautiful idea and skill constitutes a strong artistic creation. All works of art are created by this strong force.

The aesthetic education applied to the public mentioned above is generally easy for people to understand. As for the aesthetic education applied to artists, it does not seem to be easily understood by the general public. It is not that they do not understand, but that they do not pay attention. They have not paid attention to this issue. They call the aesthetic education for artists "Art Education." They call the aesthetic education applied to the public the "Aesthetic Education" that they are accustomed to using and shouting. This has created a great crime in art education: the establishment of art schools has erected a great obstacle on the road to the development of art (see my humble book "The Future of Art Schools").

The most important thing for those who implement aesthetic education is to first determine the standard of aesthetic education. Whether it is implemented on the public or on artists, as long as the initiator has considerable faith, the recipient will naturally get a considerable effect.

We can find many examples of the traces of the implementation of aesthetic education from the modern Western art countries (see "Elfo Magazine," my humble work "The Path of the Development of French Art").

First, we can see it from the organization of their public cities: regarding the organization of public cities, there are parks, memorial halls, buildings, sculptures, decorations, etc. The establishment of parks can regulate the noise of the city and cultivate the open-minded emotions of the general public. Memorial halls, buildings, sculptures, etc. can evoke a historical idea in the public and reflect the outline of a formative art in the public. In addition, there are grand art academies that can not only be enjoyed by the general public, but also be studied by artistic geniuses. Art exhibition members also have the same function. Music halls and theaters can not only enable the public to directly enjoy physiological and spiritual pleasure, but also enable artists to be greatly infected in invisible ways to complete their creations. For example, Corot's secluded emotional tone is mostly influenced by the scenery of the Paris National Music Hall (Opera), because Corot often goes to the music hall to watch dramas. There are also open-air concerts, which can enable ordinary people and proletarian artists to enjoy a considerable aesthetic intoxication and arouse the resonance of sensitive geniuses. Such beautiful and artistic environments filling the urban society are good results of the implementation of aesthetic education and good materials for implementing aesthetic education.

Second, we can see it from private residences and clothing: the residences of Westerners can be said to be aestheticized. If we look at their working class, they are all orderly, and the decoration of the living room can also do its best to embellish it. Once we enter their exquisite living room, we recall the chaos of the Chinese people and the lack of aesthetic thinking of the Chinese nation, which is indeed a clear distinction between civilization and savagery. The middle and upper class families have more magnificent villas, surrounded by gardens. The flowers and trees are in full bloom in spring and summer. Living in them is like being in paradise. Compared to those who are more wealthy, they do not hesitate to spend a lot of money to decorate their residences (the author once saw a French company customizing a complete set of living room furniture, including tables, chairs, walls, and all applied items, from the Duran Decoration Factory in France, costing more than 1.5 million French francs, about 300,000 current national currency, and it took 10 months to build this living room). It can be seen how much Westerners value and appreciate art. The author can also say that the French people's artistic hobby is often balanced with their economic situation. If we go to the Loire River area in central France to see the construction of those palaces and their internal decoration, we can know the climax of the French royal family's artistic hobby in the Middle Ages. Other ordinary people can also enjoy their aesthetic pleasures according to their economic situation. We can directly say that the French nation's "art appreciation ability" is cultivated very commonly. If we look at their clothing, especially women and children, they are all very aestheticized. Especially the patterns of the clothes in dance theaters are renewed every day, which can be said to be the best of their beauty. Their daily clothing is designed and pursued by experts all day long, and they are constantly updated. From this, we can see their love for aesthetic hobbies. However, their deep cultivation of "aesthetic consciousness" is not accidental. It is constituted by a historical and social beautification education. Their beautification education circulates with each other and helps each other, creating a firm "backbone consciousness," releasing a harmonious atmosphere for society, and opening beautiful flowers for mankind.

With the above-mentioned aesthetic environment, the French do not talk about beautifying the public, but the public will beautify themselves. They do not talk about art education, but geniuses will become artists. In French society, infants have a harmonious environment surrounding them from the time they are born, and beautiful flowers reflecting on their faces and eyelids. From childhood, they have a good family environment, and as soon as they go out, there are parks, legitimate playgrounds for entertainment, and sculptures, paintings, buildings, and all other practical decorations filling the city to attract their eyes, to stir their emotions, and to cultivate their beautiful minds.

After reading the above, we can know that the implementation of aesthetic education should create a beautiful environment and an artistic environment, such as the establishment of parks, art museums, music halls, theater construction, as well as the carving and painting decoration of all city families. In addition, the instillation of wisdom, the immersion in natural beauty, etc., are all things that people who implement aesthetic education should pay attention to. These direct or indirect environments about beauty and art are necessary tools for the implementation of aesthetic education.

Mr. Veron has a very valuable remark about aesthetic education. He said that "we should develop young people to the gardens of various beautiful emotions, and use various methods to stir up the expansion of that moral strength (Puissance Morape) that is the true source of creating art, refine their senses, arouse their fetal ideas, ignite their ideas, get close to them with general heroism, feed them with various works of art, teach them to understand the greatness of people and human society, and place them in the situation that makes them most likely to give rise to 'aesthetic sense' and 'poetic inspiration'. Finally, use various forms to often make their eyes and ears enjoy a special pleasure: a pure 'aesthetic pleasure' (Jouissance esthetipue) - see Veron's 'Aesthetics' (LEsthetipue) of style." These words are all guides for those who implement aesthetic education. We will not be wrong to base our implementation of aesthetic education on these words.

Those who have always talked about aesthetic education and implemented aesthetic education in China have paid very little attention to the broad and universal aesthetic education mentioned above. They either only talk about a few courses in drawing, music, and handicrafts in normal schools and middle schools, or they rush to open art schools. They only know how to use those teaching courses as a convenience for implementing aesthetic education. With this biased and deformed method of implementing aesthetic education, the author dares to assert that there will not be much effect in a few years. It cannot cultivate a general concept and interest in beauty among the public, nor can it enable geniuses to develop into professional artists. This method of implementing aesthetic education urgently needs to be changed.

Art World Submission Guidelines

(1) The text is limited to news, reviews, and introductions of recent art (painting, music, sculpture, architecture, drama, etc.) and literature at home and abroad.

(2) Photos are limited to recent portraits and works of domestic and foreign writers and various photographs related to the text.

(3) The number of words in each article should not exceed 2,000.

(5) Do not write on both sides of the paper.

The manuscript should be written in horizontal characters and should not be sloppy. Western texts can be omitted if possible. If it is necessary to quote the original text, it must be attached below the translation.

(7) Do not use blue ink to draw in the illustrations attached to the manuscript, and do not use colored paper. White paper and black drawings must be used.

(8) Please indicate that the manuscript should be sent to the Art World Editorial Department. (9) Manuscripts will not be returned whether they are published or not. If a return is required, it should be stated in advance and sufficient postage stamps should be attached.

(10) Remuneration for writing is divided into three types: four yuan, three yuan, and two yuan per thousand words. The same applies to each picture and photograph. If there are special manuscripts, the remuneration will be calculated separately.

Home
